Therefore, many securities have already shown a downward trend. The sudden news of the bankruptcy of a certain old store with a history of fifty-two years on Thursday caused the securities market to plummet suddenly and uncontrollably.

It is estimated that the total loss in the prices of various securities on that day reached hundreds of millions of yuan.

Domestic News

Chairman Chiang's Thesis 66

Consolidate Unity and Ensure Peace

Revealing the Two Meanings for the Whole Country to Abide By

Nanjing Telegram - Chairman Chiang published an article on the 13th entitled "Consolidating Unity and Ensuring Peace." It reads as follows:

The purpose of the National Revolution is to eliminate the warlords who bring disaster to the country, establish national unity, and implement the Three Principles of the People to advance China toward freedom and equality. This meaning is clear and known to everyone. Since the completion of the Northern Expedition, the National Government has proclaimed peaceful unification as an unchangeable policy. The people of the whole country, fearful of the war disasters that have followed since the founding of the Republic of China, are all looking forward to and supporting its realization. However, as the demobilization resolutions were just beginning to be implemented, the rebellious traces of ambitious military men were immediately revealed. From the Gui Clique's rebellion to the recent rebellions of Yan and Feng, they arose one after another, successively and fiercely, noisy and disturbing, lasting for two years. The government had no choice but to suppress the chaos to stop the chaos, and the people had no choice but to sacrifice the price to seek peace. Fortunately, the great righteousness has penetrated deep into the hearts of the people, and the soldiers are all bravely serving their lives. An unprecedented turmoil was finally quelled, and the sea and land were reunited, and peace reappeared. This war has, on the one hand, proved that our party's ideological policy truly conforms to the requirements of the whole country and that all those who seize military power and undermine unity, no matter how stubbornly they combine, will inevitably be defeated. On the other hand, it has made us aware that peace and unity are not two separate things, but are actually interconnected. Therefore, without consolidating unity, it is impossible to ensure peace, and without the whole country unanimously understanding the true meaning of peace, it is impossible to consolidate the unity of the country. In view of the eagerness of the people of the whole country for good governance, I would like to take this opportunity, at the end of this war, to first clarify this meaning to our compatriots. In modern countries, only international relations can speak of war and peace. If a country's organization is sound, there will only be the suppression of rebellions and no civil wars of mutual conflict. The so-called domestic peace is characterized by clear discipline and strong public opinion, which can use the power of the state to suppress rebellions before they take shape. Otherwise, the name of peace will have no foundation. Since the founding of the Republic of China, the people's pursuit of peace and the incomplete elimination of the revolution have allowed the warlords to flourish, each possessing their own army and territory, competing for power, and plunging the country into fragmentation. In addition, with the public opinion not being expressed, unscrupulous politicians were able to act arbitrarily and cause confusion, which allowed the struggles between groups to become a recurring story. Losing their way and forgetting to return, they regarded it as normal. Even in recent years, after the completion of unification, this absurd misconception is still deeply rooted in the hearts of the people. Even in the past two years, the central government's conquest to ensure peaceful unification has been regarded by domestic intellectuals as no different from struggles between factions. Unable to distinguish between obedience and rebellion, between good and evil, if this is not corrected, when will the national policy be determined, and how can the guarantee of peace be achieved? I deeply believe in the urgency of the people's desire for peace and seek a way to ensure peace, and I believe that the following two meanings must be deeply understood and observed by all compatriots. What are the two meanings? First, in political measures, the central government must accommodate the opinions of the people as much as possible within the scope of not violating the party's Three Principles of the People's founding principles, but it must not allow the use of force under the guise of name. Second, the foundation of unity must be maintained by the state with all its strength, and no army should be allowed to cause any slight damage. Unity is the element of a country, and the army is the force of a country. The National Revolutionary Army sacrificed countless soldiers, and its most significant achievement was to destroy individual forces and establish national forces to complete the foundation of unity. Since it is the force of the state, it should only be used for the benefit of the state. Violating this meaning is an act of rebellion. This is a very simple truth that even a three-year-old child can understand. However, the bad habits of the warlords have spread and followed each other, like toxic bacteria lurking, and they will erupt with a touch. As in the current war to suppress rebellion, all parties participating in the rebellion have actually followed the old habits of usurpation and territorial division, with unspeakable ulterior motives. They falsely accuse the country, exaggerate and embellish their words, and at the beginning of the war, they relied on the beautiful name of military remonstrance to coerce the central government. Common, fickle politicians and traitors of the party and state then took advantage of this. The people failed to see through their conspiracies early and only blamed the central government for undue tolerance, believing that peace should not be easily broken. The disaster broke out and almost became irrecoverable. In fact, whether the rebels usurp power or not, they do not have the interests of the country in mind. Even if they have genuine views on national affairs, but they use the form of armed forces, the discipline is destroyed, and the losses are great. Where can the foundation of unity be entrusted? If the people are ignorant of this meaning and only pray for peace day and night, it is like climbing a tree to catch fish, and only see their pitifulness. Furthermore, our party follows the teachings of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen, implementing political tutelage on the one hand to cultivate a strong democracy and consolidate the foundation of the Republic of China. At the same time, for the important national policies, it has always been with a public-spirited mind toward the world and praying for the cooperation of the people of the whole country. Public and private documents are available for inspection. There has never been any intention to shut the door and refuse participation of the people or refuse to accept public opinion. What it firmly believes and insists on for the people to abide by together is only the fundamental principles of the Three People's Principles and the strategies and steps shown in the teachings of the Premier, which are considered essential for nation-building and are not allowed to be discussed. Freedom of speech cannot involve the national system. This is a common rule in modern countries and should also be understood and sympathized with by all discerning scholars in the country. I believe that the biggest obstacle to domestic unrest is the elimination of traditional concepts and the failure to establish the center of thought. If it is believed that rebels can confront the central government, then the foundation of unity will be shaken. If it is believed that harming the foundation of the country is a kind of political struggle, then permanent peace will not be guaranteed. Now that the bitter experience has been vast, the people are in distress and the country is in crisis, waiting to be saved. At the beginning of this great suppression of the rebellion, there should be a thought of treading on frost and ice. Therefore, I have fully discussed the great reason why unity and peace are interconnected and the necessary conditions for its realization and have earnestly stated it to my compatriots. My compatriots should know that the people are all related to the joys and sorrows of the country. If they regard it as a matter of indifference, they will be evading their heavenly duty. From now on, regarding national political measures, as long as they do not violate the principles of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen's teachings, I hope that they will change from private discussions on the sidelines to honest criticisms. Whether it is to correct shortcomings or elaborate on opinions, the central government will be open to suggestions, choose the good and follow it. If they contribute their talents and efforts and are willing to share difficulties, then selection of talented and capable people will not be restricted by any one rule. For national unity, it is even more necessary for the whole country to be united and to use the pure public opinion of the people to provide strong support. If there are politicians who harm the country with their deceptive words and incite the military to gradually rebel, seize the central government, and undermine unity, regardless of the size of the matter, they must be punished by the strictest laws and regulations and not be treated with leniency.

To accept the strengths of all to achieve a common will, and to reform the rules to prevent the use of force is the only way to guarantee peace. I believe that the most important thing at present is to consolidate the unity of the country. Therefore, everything that can be treated with leniency, and the actions that undermine unity cannot be forgiven. Everything can be tolerated, and the path to endangering the foundation of the country must not be opened. This is what I have always cherished, and what I will continue to strive for in the future is nothing more than this. In the past, I did not care about any sacrifices to consolidate unity, and in the future, I will not make any sacrifices to guarantee peace.

I only believe that consolidating unity is the only mission to complete the National Revolution, and ensuring peace is the greatest responsibility of the National Government. Therefore, I will devote all my efforts to achieve this goal of consolidating unity and ensuring peace. Zhuge Liang said, "I will exhaust myself to the utmost, even to my death." I am the same, and I am willing to offer my foolish loyalty to repay the party and the country. However, because this matter is so important, I have taken the liberty of explaining it to my compatriots in detail.

Memorial Week at the Central Government and National Government 67

The Central Party Headquarters held its 81st weekly memorial service for the late Premier Sun Yat-sen at 9:00 AM on October 13th in the auditorium. In attendance were Central Committee members Li Shizeng, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Jingheng, Hu Hanmin, Wang Zhengting, Li Wenfan, Chen Lifu, Chen Bulei, Kexinge, and approximately five to six hundred staff members from various ministries and departments, as well as guests. Wu Jingheng presided over the ceremony. After the formalities, Wang Zhengting delivered a report, stating briefly: The rebellion of Yan and Feng this time is a misunderstanding of the Three People's Principles. The Premier's sole principle lies in

enabling the Republic of China to stand on equal footing in the world. He dedicated himself to this for forty years as if it were one day. The Yan-Feng rebellion can be said to be against China's freedom and equality, hoping to collude with foreign powers to preserve their separatist forces and rights. In terms of global trends, for a country that is divided into four or five parts to stand on equal footing with other unified countries is like trying to find fish in trees. For several months, due to the Yan-Feng rebellion, the pain and losses suffered by the country and the people, and the

sacrifices made by our front-line soldiers, are truly distressing. Fortunately, Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek led extremely loyal armed comrades to quell the great disaster. The heads of various branches of government have worked hard in the rear to maintain the interdependent relationship between politics and the military, enabling smooth progress. Peaceful unification has already been 80 or 90 percent successful, which is a great blessing for the future of the Republic of China. From the perspective of diplomacy, to achieve national freedom and equality, it is necessary to first achieve the consolidation and unification of the government. Now that the opportunity for unification has arrived, it depends on the united efforts of all the people to assist the government. As citizens, they must know that the strength of a country does not only rely on the vastness of its land and the multitude of its people. Because if the land is large, there will be people coveting its resources, easily provoking aggressive intentions. If there is no strong government to protect it, the dangers are many. In the past hundred years, China's diplomatic failures have put it in a state of constant panic. Therefore, the Premier loudly appealed to awaken the people and arouse their patriotism to preserve the legacy of our ancestors for more than four thousand years, as well as the historical and cultural

glory. The path that a country should take to achieve strength lies in being able to apply good diplomatic policies, especially in being able to

recognize the direction of world trends, and which countries treat us well and can treat us equally, and which countries adopt aggressive policies towards us and do not treat us equally. Those who can treat us equally, we should regard as good friends. Those who do not treat us equally, we should plan appropriate countermeasures. Take Russia, for example. That country shares a border with our country, and its domestic situation is similar to ours. It seems that it should have very good friendship with our country. Why is the relationship not good and diplomatic relations have not been restored to this day? Because it adopts the Third International ideology, trying to overthrow politics and human happiness around the world, wanting to assimilate China with it, imitating its actions of killing, arson, and creating a world of terror, and constantly causing trouble in China. What friendship is there to speak of? In addition, there are one or two countries that have no ambition to invade China's territory, but use commercial warfare tactics to seize China's economic power, leading to inevitable conflicts of interest. Regarding consular jurisdiction, if they are unwilling to give it up, they are using this unequal system to allow

businesses operating in China to pay less or not pay all the taxes owed to China, giving them a superior position in trade with China. Also, a country that shares our language and ethnicity seems to have better friendship with our country, but conflicts are still inevitable. Because their domestic politicians and newspaper writers are ignorant of world trends, thinking that once China becomes strong, they will be in danger. They often use our warlords to fuel our internal strife, making it impossible for the country to unify. This is a huge mistake on their part. It is hoped that they can realize this soon, improve their attitude, and join hands to advance towards the realm of strength. The most important key to diplomacy now is to recover our country's consular jurisdiction. If this can be achieved, then the work of abolishing unequal treaties will have been largely successful. Some people once

thought that tariff autonomy and the abolition of consular jurisdiction are equally

difficult. In fact, with tariff autonomy, although import goods slightly increase the burden, the ultimate bearers are the Chinese people. As the saying goes, "the wool comes from the sheep's back," the increased burden is still on the Chinese. Therefore, there is no strong opposition. However, consular jurisdiction is related to their commercial interests in China, so they are unwilling to give it up easily. The government is currently researching methods and actively proceeding, hoping that the people will unite as the government's backing to achieve this goal as soon as possible. As for the embassies of various countries, their failure to move to the capital not only causes various inconveniences in diplomacy, but also shows that various countries do not have sufficient respect for our government. No country in the world has a foreign embassy located a thousand miles away from the capital. Recently, the bogus government in Beiping (Beijing) dared to form, and they cannot help but think that having the embassies in Beiping can be used for help. The embassies may also think that the political situation in Beiping is more convenient. It is hoped that the government will conduct research and preparation so that the embassies can be moved south as soon as possible. The report concluded, and the meeting adjourned at 10:30 AM.

On the same morning at 10:00 AM, the National Government held its weekly memorial service for the late Premier Sun Yat-sen. In attendance were Chiang Kai-shek, Gu Yingfen, Zhu Peide, Wang Boqun, Wang Xiling, He Yaozu, Jiang Menglin, Wang Zhengting, Yi Peiji, Zhang Nanxian, Zhu Lühe, Lin Xiang, Wei Daoming, Liu Ruiheng, Chen Shaokuan, Chen Yu, Zhang Wohua, Zhu Jingnong, Wang Jiazhen, Zhou Yawei, Wu Siyu, and all staff members from the two offices of the National Government, totaling over three hundred people. After President Chiang performed the rituals, he gave a political report: "Today, I will briefly report on the past military situation and the future policy direction of the government. The progress of the suppression of the rebellion over the past six months has already been reported in detail. The number of deaths and injuries in this suppression of the rebellion is approximately 95,000. Countless others whose numbers cannot be verified are not included. As for the rebel army, the number of deaths and injuries must be increased by at least one-third. The total number should be above 150,000. Approximately one-third of our side died, and approximately two-thirds were injured. The rebel side had about half deaths and half injuries. According to investigations, there are already over 80,000 wounded rebel soldiers in Zhengzhou, Zhangde, and Luoyang. Other locations are not included. At the beginning of the war, we thought that Feng said he had 270,000 troops, and Yan said he had 150,000 troops, which were exaggerations. But after investigation, Feng's army was indeed more than 270,000. Because Feng recruited more than 100,000 soldiers when the war started. Feng's total army was about 400,000, and Yan's total army was about 200,000. Although Feng's and Yan's armies were numerous, they did not have enough firearms. Therefore, only one-fourth of their troops used guns, and most of the rest used broadswords and spears. Therefore, the rebel army had more casualties than us. Therefore, the total number of deaths and injuries in this battle should be over 300,000. Such a great sacrifice, whether it is our army or the enemy army, all belong to Chinese soldiers. And the enemy officers and soldiers all understand that these deaths and injuries are

extremely unjustified. Therefore, they are unwilling to fight in the future. As for the people in the war zone, countless people starved to death or came close to death, and the losses of houses and food are incalculable. The great sacrifice this time, in short, is to seek China's unification and truly achieve lasting peace. Now that the military has ended, the government's responsibility is only to consolidate unification and ensure peace

to fulfill the government's mission and responsibility. From now on, we will strive for leniency in politics. No matter what political views anyone has, as long as they do not violate the Three People's Principles and the Outline of National Reconstruction, they are free. We should try to accommodate public opinion as much as possible. Even those who previously had different political views from the government, if they do not use the military to undermine unification and peace, and have correct views, can also be accommodated as much as possible. As for the military aspect, we must strive for organization. If anyone provokes the military and causes domestic war, whether they are politicians or warlords, they will be punished as counter-revolutionaries and will not be forgiven. It is hoped that government colleagues will understand that the price paid for this sacrifice is to consolidate unification and ensure peace, and everyone should follow this intention to accomplish the mission and achieve the goal." The report concluded, and the meeting adjourned.

The Situation in Henan After the Zhengzhou Conference 68

He Yingqin Appointed to Preside Over the Zhengzhou Headquarters

70,000 Feng Troops Disarmed and Will Be Reorganized Urgent dispatch from Hankou: After the recapture of Zhengzhou, Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek moved his headquarters from Kaifeng to Zhengzhou in order to quickly resolve the situation in Henan. He convened a meeting of various generals, including the director of the Wuhan Headquarters, He Yingqin; the commander of the Second Army Corps, Liu Zhi; the commander of the Third Army Corps, He Chengjun; the commander of the Sixteenth Route Army, Xu Yuanquan; the commander of the Twenty-first Route Army, Xia Douyin; as well as Shangguan Yunxiang, Hao Mengling, and Xiao Zhichu, and other senior generals. They held consecutive meetings on the 7th and 8th. It is heard that the main decisions were: (1) To thoroughly resolve the remnants of the Feng army besieged near Xinzheng, and to eliminate the remaining enemies and miscellaneous troops in Henan; (2) To appoint He Yingqin as the director of the Zhengzhou Headquarters, with He Guoguang as the chief of staff, responsible for handling the situation in Henan; (3) To transfer He Chengjun to the director of the Wuhan Headquarters, drawing troops to engage in bandit suppression in the three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi; (4) To order Liu Zhi to quickly organize the Henan Provincial Government, investigate the disaster victims, provide effective relief, and handle the aftermath; (5) To transfer heavy troops to assist General Commander Yang Hucheng in attacking Luoyang. At that time, the divisions of Xu Yuanquan and Xiao Zhichu had been reassigned to the left wing. Xiao's division recaptured Dengfeng on the 6th, and Xu's division recaptured Luoyang on the 9th. Yang's army also occupied Xin'an. The area south of the Yellow River is completely under the control of the Central Army. As for the Feng army near Xinzheng, led by Zhang Weixi, Tian Jinkai, Feng Zhi'an, Ren Yingqi, Deng Baoshan, Shi Zhenqing, Tian Chunjie, Wang Hemin, Ni Yusheng, Zhao Fenglin, and others, numbering no less than eighty or ninety thousand, since their retreat route had been cut off, they were fully disarmed by the Central Army at dawn on the 8th. By the completion of the disarmament on the 9th, more than eight thousand people had been captured, along with approximately seven thousand guns, more than two hundred artillery pieces, and more than a thousand machine guns. The remaining Jin army on the south bank of the Yellow River, estimated to be about two regiments, was also disarmed. Others, such as Ji Hongchang, Liang Guanying, and Zhang Yinxiang, all led their troops to surrender and resumed their military positions. In summary, the Feng army suffered extremely heavy losses in this campaign and had no ability to re-enter Henan. Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek returned to Nanjing by plane on the 9th, leaving He Yingqin to be stationed in Zhengzhou. He Chengjun also approached Hubei on the 11th. Except for a portion remaining in Hankou, the staff of the headquarters are scheduled to go north in batches on the 12th and 13th. Regarding the troops transferred back to suppress bandits, He Chengjun said in Hankou that it would be six divisions and three brigades, but the exact number is unknown. (October 11th)

He Chengjun Returns to Hankou from Zhengzhou 69

Jiang Dingwen Arrives Together and Returns Home for Mourning

He Appointed Concurrently as Director of the Wuhan Headquarters

Six Divisions and One Brigade Head South to Undertake Bandit Suppression Urgent dispatch from Hankou: He Chengjun, the commander of the Third Army Corps, was ordered to take charge of the Pinghan Railway line operations. After several months of hard work, he repeatedly achieved successes. Now that the task of handling the situation in Henan has been assigned to He Yingqin stationed in Zhengzhou, he was specifically transferred back to Hubei to take charge of provincial affairs and concurrently serve as the director of the Wuhan Headquarters, commanding the bandit suppression affairs in the three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi. He set off from Zhengzhou at 10:00 AM on the 11th with Jiang Dingwen, the commander of the Second Army, by plane. They arrived in Hankou at 2:00 PM that afternoon. Representatives from various agencies and organizations welcomed them at the Wangjiadun Airport, including the acting chairman of the provincial government, Wu Xingya; the director of the Finance Department, Zhang Guanshi; the director of the Construction Department, Fang Dazhi; the director of the Education Department, Huang Jianzhong; committee members Xie Lü, Peng Jieshi, and Xiong Bingkun; the mayor of Hankou City, Liu Wendao; the counselors of the Headquarters, Leng Xin and Wang Shi; the committee members of the provincial party headquarters, Zuo Duo and Yu Yuzhi; the committee members of the municipal party headquarters, Liu Yun and Bi Ruoxu; as well as the commander of the Twenty-first Route Army, Xia Douyin; the commander of the Fifty-first Division, Fan Shisheng; the commander of the Thirteenth Division, Zhu Huaibing; the chief of staff of the Garrison Command, Ye Peng; the fortress commander, Yin Zusheng, and other students from various schools, totaling more than five thousand people. The Guerrilla Brigade of the Garrison Command, the Water Police Bureau, and the Third Security Brigade were responsible for security. At 2:00 PM, the plane arrived and landed. After He and Jiang disembarked, they greeted the welcomers one by one. He went to the Third Army Corps' garrison office, and Jiang went to Liu Qiyan's private residence, where they separately met with guests. They immediately telegraphed Nanjing to Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek and Shenyang to Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang, as well as telegraphing the director of the Zhengzhou Headquarters, He Yingqin, reporting their arrival in Hankou. When He and Jiang disembarked, the reporters immediately presented their cards to pay their respects and had brief talks with them, which are recorded as follows:

He Chengjun said briefly: "I have been ordered to suppress the rebellion, operating on the Pinghan and Longhai lines for seven months. Fortunately, with the prestige of the Central Government, the remaining enemies have been gradually eliminated. The Longhai front has reached Lanfeng and Kaifeng, and the right wing of the Pinghan line has fortunately been successful. The left wing has also successively occupied Luoyang and Xin'an. The central route has recaptured Zhengzhou and Xinzheng. The Feng army in Henan has been completely annihilated. Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek returned to Nanjing on the 9th and entrusted the responsibility of handling the situation in Henan and ending the war to Director He Yingqin, establishing the Zhengzhou Headquarters to handle military aftermath. The position of director of the Wuhan Headquarters is entrusted to my brothers to temporarily take charge. After returning to Hankou, my first task is to continue after Director He to handle the pacification of the three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi, with the aim of completely eliminating bandits and communists within three months, so that the people can live and work in peace. As for the troops responsible for pacification, in addition to the original garrison troops, Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek has approved the transfer of large forces from the front lines to the south. As for the Hubei Provincial Government, because I have been serving on the front lines, I have been unable to take care of it. Fortunately, with the acting chairmanship of Director Wu Xingya and the efforts of various committee members, there have been no shortcomings. In the future, I will continue to work with Director Wu and the committee members to achieve the goal of political prosperity and the happiness of the people."

Jiang Dingwen said briefly: "I was previously stationed in Wuhan and received the support of all sectors. The relationship between the military and the people was extremely harmonious. When Yan and Feng rebelled, and the Central Government used Zhang for punishment, my troops were ordered to participate in the war, first opening the Pinghan line, and then transferred to the Longhai line. After dozens of battles, large and small, we repeatedly defeated stubborn enemies. When the fighting was fierce, my father died of illness in my hometown. Military affairs detained me, and I was unable to return home. Now, most of the Yan rebel army has been eliminated. A part of the Feng rebel army has been disarmed by our army, and a part has surrendered to our army. Units such as Ji Hongchang and Liang Guanying have all been reorganized in accordance with orders and transferred to the Guangshan and Gushi areas to undertake bandit suppression. From then on, domestic warlords can be expected to be eliminated, and the Central Government's policy of peaceful unification can be realized. I took this opportunity to present a request to Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek to return home for mourning. I will stay in Hankou for one day and tomorrow morning (the 12th) will

take a plane to Nanjing and then to Zhejiang." (October 13th)

Han Fuqu Sends Representatives to Pan 70

Dispatch from Jinan: Shandong Province Chairman Han Fuqu has now sent Director of the Agriculture and Mines Department Wang Fangting as his representative to Shenyang to negotiate important matters with the Northeast Commander-in-Chief Zhang Xueliang. Wang has already taken several attendants and soldiers and gone north. The reporter visited Wang on the train. Wang said that Chairman Han immediately wanted to send a representative to Shenyang after responding to Commander Zhang's clever telegram to exchange views. Recently, Commander-in-Chief Wang Xiangting (Wang Changyu) was ordered by Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek to be a representative to Pan. Han Wang had a very close relationship with Wang and had invited him by telegram to pass through Jinan on the way, but Commander Wang passed through Qingdao due to time constraints, so he went directly to Dalian and then to Shenyang. Recently, a telegram came from Shenyang saying that they were waiting in Shenyang and asked to send a representative to meet and talk. The chairman appointed me as a representative because I am an old friend of Wang. It is expected that I will stay in Shenyang for two weeks. When the reporter asked about the mission of this trip, Wang said that it was a normal reciprocation and that there was

no so-called mission. However, according to other sources, Shandong and the Northeast need to exchange views with the Northeast authorities and make practical connections on the issue of the Qingdao naval defense area and the joint defense between Dezhou and Sangyuan in northern Shandong. This is one of the missions Wang is responsible for. Also, Shi Yousan's troops have surrendered to the Central Government. Shi recently sent a telegram to Han, expressing deep regret for the past and expressing his willingness to listen to Han's command and asking him to intercede with the Central Government. In terms of Han's friendship with Shi, Han cannot but make an effort. However, Shi's troops have now retreated to Hebei Province and have entered the Northeast defense area. In the future, if the Central Government allows the request and Shi's troops are transferred, it is necessary to contact the Northeast to avoid misunderstandings. This is also one of Wang's missions.

The Tragedy of the "Da Guangdong" Steamer in Shantou 71

One Chinese Worker Killed and Six Injured

All Sectors Resolve on Five Negotiation Methods Dispatch from Shantou: The French steamer "Da Guangdong" arrived in Shantou Port from Saigon on the 3rd. While anchoring, the partners of various inns in Shantou City boarded boats one after another to greet merchants, using bamboo hooks to climb onto the side of the steamer. The French owner of the "Da Guangdong" steamer initially ordered Annamese sailors to open water hoses to spray the inn partners, and then directed the sailors to beat Cai Yuqin, a partner of the Yi Hua Inn, to death and throw the body into the sea, and beat worker Deng Diangui and six others, who are now receiving treatment at the Municipal Hospital. Fortunately, when the incident occurred, the water police immediately boarded the ship to mediate, rescued the injured Chinese workers, and detained the Chinese comprador Chen Xianghe. According to Chen Xianghe's confession at the police station, the above-mentioned incident did occur on the day the ship arrived, but it had nothing to do with him personally. After this case occurred, the French Consul stationed in Shantou, Ouren, repeatedly asked the municipal government to release Chen Xianghe, but the municipal government refused to release him temporarily until the case was properly resolved. The Shantou branch of the Guangdong General Labor Union telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 5th, requesting that a serious negotiation be proposed to France and ordering all workers to stop working on the ship to avoid danger. Therefore, the ship repeatedly raised flags in Shantou to ask for fresh water and unload goods, but no Chinese workers responded. On the 4th, French Consul Ouren again negotiated with the municipal government, claiming that Cai Yuqin's death was due to his accidental hooking of the iron handle, injuring his head and falling into the sea, and that the workers were also injured by being sprayed by water hoses. The municipal government then sent Secretary Rao Shiyi to invite Ouren to personally visit the Municipal Hospital to examine the injured, proving that they were indeed injured by iron bars, and the bruises had not faded. The French Consul instructed the injured to take good care of themselves, and all medical expenses would be borne by him. Yesterday, a joint meeting of various labor unions in Shantou resolved on five items: (1) Punish the murderer; (2) Formally apologize to our government; (3) Compensate the injured for medical expenses; (4) Compensate the families of the deceased for pensions; (5) The French Consul should guarantee that this will not happen again in the future. After the resolution, the municipal government was requested to negotiate with the French Consul. Also, before this case is resolved, the "Da Guangdong" steamer cannot leave Shantou. French Consul Ouren sent a letter to the municipal government, stating that the "Da Guangdong" steamer suffered heavy losses due to its stay in Shantou, and specifically asked the municipal government to release the ship first, and he was willing to be responsible for a clear settlement. The "Da Guangdong" steamer then left Shantou for Hong Kong on the 5th. On the 6th, Cai Yuqin's body floated up on the opposite bank of Mashiyu at the Shantou port mouth. The body has been recovered and examined by the authorities before being submitted for negotiation. Currently, all sectors in Shantou are extremely indignant. The Shantou branch of the Guangdong General Labor Union is scheduled to convene a representative conference of all labor unions in the city at the Municipal Party Department Auditorium on the 7th to discuss everything in order to achieve the above-mentioned five requirements. (October 7th)

Wu Chao-shu's Speech at the League of Nations 72

Geneva Dispatch: During the Eleventh International League Assembly this year, Mr. Wu Chao-shu, the Chinese envoy, delivered a lengthy speech at the Assembly on September 16. The original text is recorded below.

As the time for concluding the discussion of the report draws near, I shall speak briefly. However, before discussing the League's work report for the past year, I must fulfill my duty of expressing grief. China deeply regrets the passing of Lord Balfour (former British Prime Minister), Mr. Stresemann (former German Foreign Minister), and Mr. Nansen (former Norwegian explorer). These three were great figures of the League, dedicated to the cause of peace, the aims of the League of Nations, and humanitarianism. Their contributions were immense. Now that these wise men have passed away, it is not only a loss to their nations but also a misfortune for the League and the world.

In the past year, cooperation between China and the League in matters of public health has been realized, with particular attention to port sanitation, ship inspection, and medical education. This cooperation has gradually shown good results. The personnel dispatched to China by the League have been very helpful. Regarding the mutual reporting of information on various diseases, China has also cooperated with the Far Eastern Health Bureau established by the League's Health Section in Singapore. All of this represents the initial tangible cooperation between our government and the League, which is sufficient to arouse China's attention to the League and increase China's confidence that the League can assist its member states with sincerity and integrity.

This year's Assembly should discuss the important issue of reorganizing the Secretariat. I take this opportunity to express my admiration for Sir Eric Drummond, the Secretary-General, for his outstanding talent and diligence in serving the League since its establishment. The loyalty and achievements of other officials in the Secretariat are also commendable. Since the founding of the League, its work has greatly increased, as has the work of the Secretariat. However, the organization of the Secretariat has not progressed in tandem with the expansion of its work. Therefore, if criticisms of the Secretariat's organization from various quarters, both inside and outside the Secretariat, are justified, the Chinese delegation will consider them together with the delegations of other countries to ensure that its organization is as efficient as its staff.

Another important matter to be studied by this Assembly is the amendment of the Covenant to align it with the Pact of Paris (Kellogg-Briand Pact). This pact is inextricably linked to the names of French Foreign Minister Briand and former U.S. Secretary of State Kellogg. Ten years since the Covenant came into effect, member states believe that all clauses related to war in the Covenant should and must be deleted. This demonstrates the progress of peace. I firmly believe that this move is very important, and I believe we can congratulate each other. China participated in the work of the committee to amend the Covenant, and its report is now before you. China naturally approves of the amendment. We also hope that the amendment can be implemented as soon as possible. If implemented, observing the Covenant and the Pact of Paris working in concert is truly interesting and enlightening. The Pact provides moral encouragement to the Covenant, while the Covenant provides substantive force and backing to the Pact.

Finally, I would like to discuss the plan for a European Union. This plan is also closely linked to French Foreign Minister Briand. As a non-European and representing a country whose area, population, and complexity of problems are equal to those of all of Europe, speaking from this position, the Chinese delegation believes that the plan for a European Union and the League of Nations need not be inherently incompatible. If a European Union is successfully established, it can only be a local or regional agreement within the framework of the League of Nations.

The Chinese delegation also believes that a European Union does not inherently conflict with non-European countries or groups of non-European countries. I was very interested in the speech given by Austrian Chancellor Schober some days ago on the issue of a European Union. Chancellor Schober proposed that this plan should first be implemented in groups of European countries, and then the groups should merge to achieve the goal of a pan-European Union. If this idea is ultimately adopted, I would like to extrapolate on future developments. Countries can combine themselves into groups, as Chancellor Schober argued, and these groups can then be united again in due course. The reasons for this are generally geographical, ethnic, cultural, and economic. Their organization may be for relief purposes, political purposes, or both. I dare not predict the number or names of these unions at this time. However, a European Union would certainly be one of them. Furthermore, if these unions were to solidify into an all-encompassing entity, a great world federation, would that be a fantasy? I would like to translate and recite a chapter from a Chinese classic for you. This chapter expresses the ideal of Confucius 2,400 years ago, which is still relevant to our discussion today. Confucius said: "When the Great Way prevails, the world is for all. The virtuous and capable are selected. Sincerity is cultivated, and harmony is promoted. People do not cherish only their own parents, nor do they love only their own children. The elderly are provided for until their end, the strong are employed, the young are nurtured to grow, and the widowed, orphaned, lonely, and disabled are all cared for. Men have spouses, and women have homes. People despise the waste of resources but do not hoard them for themselves. They detest the lack of effort but do not exert it solely for their own benefit. Therefore, conspiracies are suppressed and do not arise, and theft and banditry do not occur, so outer doors are not closed. This is called the Great Unity." This chapter was written in the sixth century B.C. Up to the present, Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the founder of the Republic of China, has repeatedly emphasized it. This is not a utopian ideal. Consider, twenty years ago, who could have dreamed that more than fifty countries would have a permanent meeting in Geneva, with a permanent Secretariat? Two years ago, how many people could have foreseen that responsible politicians from twenty-seven countries would be discussing the plan for a European Union, not the question of whether it was possible, but how to realize it? However, please do not be alarmed. I am not proposing a plan for a world federation. I merely wish to suggest something to you. Among our friends, one person may build a house with one floor for his own use. Later, as his circumstances improve and his family grows, he plans to add several more floors to it. He consults an architect, who says that the foundation of the original house is too weak to support the added building and must be completely rebuilt from the ground up. I now suggest to you, who are the architects of the European Union, do not repeat this mistake. When you build the European Union, do not only consider today's needs, but also plan for future use. Lay a foundation that is deep, broad, and solid so that future builders can continue to add floors, not only to accommodate the European Union but also the unions of other continents. Then the principle of the Great Unity of humankind will be within reach.

Local Correspondence Jinshan 74

Robberies in Lüxiang and Langxia (1) On the evening of the 11th of this month, around 8 PM, about fifty to sixty bandits suddenly arrived in Lüxiang, all armed with guns. After arriving in the town, they immediately divided into sections to guard the area and successively robbed shops. The heaviest losses were suffered by Yao Jinmao, Ma Hengchang Silk Shop, Zhengda, Gongda, Yuda Rice Shop, and Zhou Dachang Bran Shop. Shops such as Zhang Wanxiang, Gu Hengmao, and Sun Shengyuan also suffered considerable losses. Before leaving, the bandits threatened to rob again after the rents for the rich households' rice were collected. They left towards the west after about several hours. (2) On the same evening, about twenty bandits arrived in Langxia. The biggest loss was suffered by Tongtai Rice Shop, and one apprentice (from Songyin) was killed. Because the telephone has not been repaired, details are unknown. Currently, all the shops in Lüxiang are temporarily closed due to excessive losses. The government has no concrete measures. County Magistrate Lu Quan is resting in his hometown and has not come to Jinshan. The reason is unknown. Lüxiang has been robbed three times in a row. The people are constantly extorted, burned, and looted by bandits. Those responsible for the area are acting as if they haven't heard anything and are telling their superiors that the bandits have been suppressed. Who are they deceiving?

Successive Kidnappings in Hengjing Township Cha Shouting's family, a villager from Beigang Village, Shidu, Hengjing Township, was suddenly attacked by more than twenty bandits around 10 PM on the (12th) night. Before leaving, they kidnapped Cha's wife, Jin, and Cha's nephew, Jin Shouyi, together.

Telephone Price Increase Resolved The Suzhou Telephone Bureau received an order from the Ministry of Communications to increase the monthly telephone rental fee by two yuan starting in September. After receiving the order, Director Zhao immediately notified the General Chamber of Commerce. The Chamber of Commerce then convened a meeting of representatives from various industries to discuss the matter and submitted a request to the Ministry to temporarily waive the increase. After repeated visits to the Ministry of Communications, the approval was denied. Therefore, the Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to Director Zhao Chuanyu to discuss the matter, assuming that they would be allowed to increase the fee by one yuan per month. However, the Ministry disapproved again. Director Zhao then went to Beijing recently to meet with Minister Wang in person, explaining the difficult situation of the business community. Minister Wang then approved a temporary increase of one yuan. Starting from January of the 20th year [of the Republic], the original agreement to increase the fee by two yuan must be followed. Currently, the Suzhou Telephone Bureau has received orders to issue receipts and collect fees from users.

Another Robbery Case in the Seventh District Xu Adixin, a villager in Guandi Bridge Dahetou Fang, which is about three li east of Zhangjing Bridge (Huai'an City) in the seventh district of the county, and his younger brother Xu Adixin lived together in one room. They have been farmers and are considered a well-to-do family. Unexpectedly, around 10 PM ten days ago, more than ten bandits suddenly came, speaking in the local dialect, wearing short clothes, and carrying hard wooden sticks, flashlights, and other weapons. They broke into the house, first tied up the Xu brothers with ropes, and then looted extensively for half an hour before carrying the loot out and escaping. After inspection, it was found that more than eighty yuan in cash, more than seventy pieces of silk cloth, about one tael of gold rings and bracelets, and thirty pieces of silverware were taken, totaling a loss of more than five hundred yuan. All the field deeds (estimated to be about forty mu) were found, torn up, and looted by the bandits.

Changzhou 78

Bandits Harassing the Northern Township The Shangyan Village in the first district of the northern township of Wujin has more than eighty households and is equipped with two self-defense rifles and one pistol. At about 6 PM on the evening of the 10th, Lu Dahai and Zhou Gensheng, the bandit leaders from Tianguo Village and Zhoujiatou (Jiangyin border) near the village, joined forces with Gao Xiaosheng and Yang Xiaoda, the bandit leaders from the northern section, and led more than sixty bandits, each carrying guns, to Shang District Town, divided up the looting and also forcibly took away the hidden guns. At that time, Ge Qingda, the son of Ge Qingda, the head of Fucheng Township, was kidnapped. Before leaving, he instructed Ge Qingda to send four quick guns from the village to Guo Village at 6 AM on the 12th, and then his son would be released. During the robbery, villagers reported to the County Public Security Bureau. County Magistrate Wu immediately asked Regiment Commander Wu of the Military Police to send the Eighth Company of the Second Battalion and the Police Business Corps Patrol Team to pursue and suppress the bandits. When they arrived, the bandits had already retreated. Company Commander Fang Yongxiuquan immediately divided the teams into two branches, the first branch searched Guo Village, and the second branch searched Zhoujiatou. They set out at 5 AM on the 12th. In Guo Village, they captured eleven people with suspicious behavior, including Li Ronglin. In Zhoujiatou, the second branch captured five bandits, including Li Guochuan. During the search, gunshots were suddenly heard in the rice fields, and many bandits were seen crossing the river and fleeing. The soldiers and police immediately opened fire, and several bandits were hit. One bandit was shot in the head and fell into the river and died. The villagers fished him out, cut off his head, and asked Company Commander Fang to order the city to lead the way. Then, they also picked up a Mauser rifle left behind by the bandits and a large pile of clothes left behind when crossing the river, and all of them, together with the head, were sent to the city. After the bandits retreated, they invaded Pan City Town again at 12 PM on the 12th. Li Zongfan, the captain of the police detachment stationed in the town, immediately opened fire with them. Due to the disparity in numbers, squad leader Wang Baosheng was shot and killed, and squad member Wang Zhenhua was also injured. The team's bed tents, clothes, and other items were all burned down. A rifle was looted. Captain Li retreated to Longhutang and used the telephone to report to the county government. Around 5 PM, County Magistrate Wu again asked the Military Police Regiment to send a team to the countryside to pursue and suppress the bandits. As of the morning of the 13th, the news was still being searched.

President of Labor University Issue 85

The Ministry of Education Discusses the Receiving Method

The accounts will be checked together with the Audit Court. Teachers and staff telegraphed to request the speedy appointment of a president. Nanjing, 13th. The Ministry of Education is currently planning what method to use to receive the Labor University. However, it has asked the Audit Court to send personnel to jointly investigate the school's accounts.

Yesterday, the newspapers reported that the Ministry of Education would send people to receive and directly manage the Labor University for one year without appointing a president. The teachers and staff of the school believe that this kind of method is not the attitude that the educational authorities should take, so they telegraphed the Central Government and the founder of the school to express their opinions. The full text of the telegram is as follows: To the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Education, it is reported that the Ministry of Education will send people to receive and directly manage the Labor University for one year without appointing a president. This method has no precedent to follow and is easy to cause misunderstandings from the outside world. It does not seem to be the attitude that the educational administration authorities should have towards a national university. The teachers and students of Labor University feel uneasy and should cancel the receiving method and appoint a successor president immediately to take responsibility and avoid problems. The future of Labor Education is deeply beneficial. Cheng Ganyun, Peng Xiang, Ma Shouzhen, Li Wenying, Gong Xianming, Peng Jinyun, Hu Bin, and other teachers and staff of the Labor University, one hundred and fifty-one people, kowtowed together.

Annual Meeting of the China Cooperative Society (2) 86

Third Day's Situation The second meeting on the 12th was the third day of the opening of the China Cooperative Society's annual meeting. The morning was the second general affairs meeting, with the agenda being the reading of papers, amendment of the charter, and election of staff.

Reading of Papers This time, the society received more than twenty papers. Due to time constraints, it was impossible to read them all. Among the important papers were: 1. The Basis for the Success of Agricultural Cooperation (Wang Shiying), 2. Agricultural Cooperation Promotes the Peasant Movement (Tang Qizi), 3. Agricultural Cooperativization (Tong Yumin), 4. Suggestions for Establishing the China Cooperative Association (Wang Zhixin), 5. How to Develop China's Cooperative Enterprise (Tan Changkai), 6. Developing China's Export Trade with the Cooperative System (Hou Houpei), 7. Cooperation and Legislation (Wu Yuzhang), 8. The Profit View of Cooperativism (Hou Zhe'an), 9. Cooperatives and Economic Rationalization (Shou Miancheng), 10. Research on Rotating Credit Associations in China's Cooperative System (Wang Zongpei), 11. An Analysis of the Rochdale Principles of Cooperatives (Cheng Junqing), 12. A Review of China's Cooperative Enterprise (Song Xixiang), 13. In addition, there were papers by Xu Shuji, Wu Juenong, Chen Zhongming, etc., which were not included because the topics were unknown.

Amending the Charter The society's original charter was very simple. Council members Chen Zhongming, Hou Houpei, Wu Yuzhang, and others proposed amendments. After two hours of discussion, a new charter of forty articles was passed, with changes made to the internal organization and the number of executive committee members.

Electing Staff Next was the re-election of seven executive committee members. The results were: Zhang Shiying 40 votes, Chen Guofu 38 votes, Chen Zhongming 28 votes, Yu Jingtang 27 votes, Xu Shaodi 26 votes, Hou Houpei 24 votes, Tang Qizi and Wang Zhixin 20 votes each. They were elected as executive committee members. Because Tang Qizi and Wang Zhixin received the same number of votes, a drawing was used to decide the result. Wang Zhixin was elected as a formal executive committee member, and Tang Qizi was a reserve member. In addition to Mr. Tang, Wu Juenong and Zhang Tinghao were also reserve members.

The Zhejiang Provincial Party Department's Banquet The Zhejiang Provincial Party Department hosted a banquet for the society's members at the Young Men's Christian Association Western Restaurant at noon on the 12th. Chairman Fang Qingru gave a welcome speech, followed by a response speech by Wang Zhixin, representing the society, and a speech by Tong Yumin. That same evening, the Zhejiang Provincial Women's Sericulture Training Institute, the Agricultural College of Zhejiang University, the Provincial Advanced Sericulture School, and the Provincial Sericulture Improvement Center jointly hosted a banquet for the society's members at the Jufeng Garden in West Lake. The atmosphere was lively, and the gathering ended happily at 10 p.m.

Chen Shizhen Resigns from Concurrent Position as Director of Social Education Department 87

Yang Lian Succeeds as Director of the Department of Social Affairs Chen Shizhen, a counselor of the Ministry of Education, since concurrently serving as the acting director of the Department of Social Education, in addition to handling daily official duties, has also strived to plan the implementation of national mass education. However, because Mr. Chen's physical constitution is inherently weak and it is difficult for him to concurrently handle such busy duties for a long time, he has repeatedly requested Minister Jiang to allow him to resign from his concurrent position as director of the Department of Social Affairs so that he can concentrate on his duties as a counselor and fulfill his previous agreement (Mr. Chen, when taking on the concurrent position, expressed that he would temporarily act for two months and asked the minister to take his time to find a dedicated person to take on the position). Recently, it has been heard that Minister Jiang, considering Mr. Chen's sincere intention to resign, has internally decided to approve his resignation from his concurrent position as director of the Department of Social Affairs. As for the successor, it has also been internally decided that Yang Lian, who is currently inspecting education in Europe, will succeed to this position. He will soon submit a request to the Executive Yuan to be forwarded to the National Government for appointment. According to reports, Yang Lian is a graduate of Peking University and has served as the director of academic affairs at Zhejiang Provincial First Middle School. At the First National Education Conference, Mr. Yang represented Zhejiang Province and strongly advocated for the merger of normal schools, co-education, and the abolition of classical Chinese in elementary schools. Last winter, Zhejiang Province sent him to Europe and the United States to study education. After arriving in the United States, Mr. Yang majored in educational administration at Columbia University. He has now arrived in Europe for inspection and recently sent a telegram to the capital stating that he is expected to return to China in one or two months.

Orchid Society Holds 20th Anniversary Meeting 88

The Orchid Society, an organization of Chinese students studying in the United States, has a history of twenty years. It was initially established in 1910 with its headquarters in New York, later moved to Peiping. At the same time, branches were established in six major cities in the United States, including New York, Philadelphia, Chicago, and Boston, as well as in Tianjin, Shanghai, Guangzhou, and other places in China. Starting from October 10th, a three-day meeting was held in Wuxi. Attendees included Xu Zhendong, He Jiecai, Cao Yunxiang, Zheng Xiangheng, Cheng Yingzhang, Luo Yuming, Zhang Xianglin, Ma Mingyun, Gu Fugao, Niu Huisheng, Tang Rongtao, Zhu Bin, Yang Xiaobo, Zhou Qibang, Ruan Runsu, Chen Wencan, Wei Zengfu, Shen Zongkang, Chen Huayin, Xie Songsan, Pan Xuean, Wu Shuchang, Wang Hua, Ye Guixin, etc. Minister of Finance Song Ziwen, a member of the society, also came to Wuxi to participate. The meeting's three-day itinerary was as follows:

Day 1: Visited Huishan Mountain and the Second Spring Under Heaven, and toured Qin Garden. Returned to the city for dinner in the evening. Opened the society's affairs meeting at 7:30 p.m. Day 2: Visited the scenic spots along the lake. Left for the Jinghu area in the afternoon.

Local News

Municipal Government Approves Two Education Regulations 89

In order to enhance the teaching effectiveness of elementary school teachers in Shanghai, the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau has specially formulated a regulation for in-service training of elementary school teachers. In addition, in order to take into account the livelihood of private tutors in the city and the studies of children, it has also formulated a regulation for the assessment of private tutors. It is now heard that these two regulations have been submitted to the municipal government for approval and are specially recorded as follows:

1. Regulations for In-Service Training of Elementary School Teachers 90

Article 1: The Bureau has formulated the Regulations for In-Service Training of Municipal Elementary School Teachers in order to enhance the teaching effectiveness of municipal elementary school teachers. Article 2: The duration of in-service training for elementary school teachers is tentatively set at five years. Article 3: The methods of in-service training for elementary school teachers are temporarily divided into the following items: 1. Summer school, 2. Training courses, 3. Public lectures, 4. Subject-specific teaching seminars, 5. Assigned self-study subjects, 6. Circulating reading materials, 7. Observation. Article 4: All municipal elementary school teachers who have graduated from university, higher normal school, or high school education programs must attend summer school for two years within five years (designated as the second and fourth years). Article 5: All municipal elementary school teachers who have graduated from secondary schools and simple normal schools or passed the qualification examination must attend summer school for three years within five years (designated as the first, third, and fifth years). Article 6: If an elementary school teacher fails more than two-fifths of the subjects they are studying after taking the examination at summer school, they should retake them at the next summer school or take a supplementary examination on the subjects they should study, as designated by the Bureau. Article 7: If an elementary school teacher's failing subjects account for less than two-fifths of the teaching time of the subjects they are studying after taking the examination at summer school, they may take a make-up examination in the first semester of that year. If they still fail, they should retake them at the next summer school or take a supplementary examination on the subjects they should study, as designated by the Bureau. Article 8: During other years when elementary school teachers do not attend summer school, the Bureau will designate at least one self-study subject each year and hold examinations on a regular basis. Those who fail will be ordered by the Bureau to take a make-up examination or retake the course. Article 9: Elementary school teachers should regularly visit school education or other educational institutions, but they must submit an application to the Bureau for approval in advance and report the situation after the visit for future reference. Article 10: Elementary school teachers should give two public lectures in each semester through the local education association and must submit a report to the Bureau for future reference in advance. Article 11: Elementary school teachers should attend subject-specific teaching seminars. Article 12: Elementary school teachers should complete the assigned circulating reading materials within a specified period and submit their research results to the principals of their respective schools for compilation and submission for future reference. Article 13: If an elementary school teacher has one of the following circumstances, the Bureau will give appropriate punishment: A. Failure to attend summer school without reason and failure to report as required; B. Failure to attend summer school for a reason and failure to apply to the Bureau for approval; C. Failing subjects account for more than two-fifths of the subjects taken at summer school for two consecutive times; D. Failure to effectively implement the various in-service training methods stipulated in Article 3 of these Regulations. The punishment methods in the preceding paragraph are temporarily set as warning, non-promotion, demotion, and suspension from duty. Article 14: All newly appointed elementary school teachers should follow these Regulations from the year they start their service. Article 15: If an elementary school teacher has works related to in-service training that are submitted and reviewed by the Bureau and are confirmed to have publication value, they may be handled in accordance with the Bureau's rules for soliciting contributions for series of books and will be given appropriate awards. The awards in the preceding paragraph are temporarily divided into several items, such as honorary award, promotion, and exemption from assessment for one term. Article 16: Elementary school teachers who have completed the five-year in-service training period and passed the examination will be given a first-term in-service training certificate. Article 17: These Regulations shall be implemented after being submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and promulgated.

2. Regulations for Assessment of Private Tutors Article 1: The assessment and certification of private tutors in this city shall be handled in accordance with these Regulations. Article 2: Anyone who wishes to teach in a private school in this city, except those who have already passed the registration and review of elementary school teachers by the Bureau, should be subject to examination and certification. Article 3: Those who are subject to assessment should fill in their name, gender, age, place of origin, resume, and private school address on the registration form and submit it to the Bureau, along with two recent 2.5-inch half-length photos of themselves. Article 4: The date of registration and assessment will be announced by the Bureau in the Min Guo Daily and the Xin Shen Daily. Article 5: The examination and assessment are divided into three items: written examination, oral examination, and physical examination. Article 6: Those who pass the various examinations and assessments in the preceding paragraph after review by the Bureau will be issued a certificate of assessment. Article 7: The validity period of the certificate of assessment is set at two years. Article 8: If there are any matters not covered in these Regulations, they may be submitted to the Municipal Government for amendment at any time. Article 9: These Regulations shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Fudan University 25th Anniversary Celebration 96

To be Held for Three Days Starting from the 16th Fudan University in Shanghai will hold its 25th anniversary celebration for three days starting on the 16th of this month. On the second day (the 17th), guests and alumni will be received at the university in Jiangwan in the morning, followed by a lunch. A ceremony will be held at 2 p.m. in the afternoon. The past history and current situation of the university are briefly described as follows:

——Past History—— Seven years before the founding of the Republic of China, some teachers and students of the Aurora College, feeling that religious academics should not be confused, resolutely left the school and created Fudan Public School.

Zhou Fu, the Governor-General of Liangjiang, allocated the former Wusong Navy Commander's Office as the school site. The school was established in accordance with the regulations of the Qing Dynasty's higher schools, and Ma Liang was publicly appointed as the president. A middle school was also attached, and many scholars and Confucian scholars came to study at the time. Two years later, Yan Fu succeeded him. He then asked Governor-General Duanfang to approve the establishment of the school and allocate 2,000 yuan per month for official expenses. Later, Zhang Renjun succeeded as Governor-General of Liangjiang and reallocated more than 70 mu of official land in Wusong to prepare for the construction of school buildings, with Xia Jingguan as the president. After more than a year, Xia left and Gao Guqian, the Jiangsu Education Commissioner, succeeded him. A year later, Gao left and Ma Liang became president again. During this period, four classes graduated from the higher regular program, with a total of 57 graduates. During the Xinhai Revolution, the school buildings were borrowed by the Songhu Military Headquarters, and the students were scattered and the music stopped. In the first year of the Republic of China, Yu Youren, Hu Dunfu, and others from the alumni association traveled to Shanghai and Nanjing to jointly plan the restoration of the school. They submitted a request to the Nanjing Provisional Government to approve a subsidy of 10,000 yuan, and Cai Yuanpei, the Minister of Education, approved the establishment of the school. They also submitted a request to the authorities in Jiangsu and Shanghai to allocate the Li Gong Ancestral Hall in Xujiahui as the school site. Many people, including school directors Sun Yat-sen, Wang Liangchou, Chen Ying, and Cheng Xuelou, wholeheartedly supported the school. Ma Liang was still publicly appointed as the president. Later, Ma was summoned to Beijing, and Li Denghui, the former Dean of Academic Affairs, succeeded him. Renowned figures in Shanghai were then gathered to form a board of directors to provide assistance in various ways, which helped to maintain the school. Later, as the number of students increased day by day, it was decided to build school buildings and start a university. Since the official land in Wusong was not entirely suitable, more than 70 mu of land were successively purchased in Jiangwan, and enthusiastic supporters of education at home and abroad actively donated money. More than 300,000 yuan was collected successively. Several people independently donated money to build school buildings, such as Guo Zibin, who independently built the Zibin Yuan, worth more than 70,000 yuan, and the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company, which independently built the Jian Gong Hall, worth more than 50,000 yuan. Huang Yizhu independently built a school building, worth more than 15,000 yuan. From June 9th to October 19th, dormitories, gymnasiums, libraries, sanatoriums, and other facilities were successively built, and all equipment was modeled after Europe and America. In the spring of 11th, the university department was first moved in, and the middle school department was still operated at the original site in Xujiahui. In 13th, President Li requested a leave of absence to travel south, and Guo Renyuan acted as the president, opening the College of Psychology and attaching the Experimental Middle School. In the spring of 14th, President Li returned to China, and the board of directors elected Guo Renyuan as the vice president. He resigned in the summer of 16th. From the 8th year of the Republic of China to the summer of the 19th year, a total of 1,189 students graduated from various departments of the university.

Du Xigui to Return to Shanghai 108

Has Already Taken the Zhaoguo Maru Mail Ship to Return Home

Having completed his mission of inspecting naval affairs, he is returning home at full speed and has safely arrived in Tokyo, Japan. Nagai's Mission to Beijing 109

Shigemitsu Goes to Beijing First to Introduce Him The Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Nagai Ryutaro, is scheduled to arrive in Beijing on the afternoon of the 16th to meet with Chairman Chiang and the Minister of Foreign Affairs, etc. The Japanese Chargé d'Affaires, Shigemitsu Aoi, went to Beijing on the evening of the 13th to introduce him.
