Therefore, Nagai was sent to China for inspection. As for the issue of extraterritoriality, it cannot be shelved for too long, so he is also taking this opportunity to exchange opinions with our diplomatic authorities in advance.

Large Quantities of Japanese Rice Shipped to Shanghai 110

The Mitsukeyama Maru Will Arrive in a Day or Two

The Azumayama Maru Will Continue to Transport Rice After a bumper autumn harvest in Japan this year, the Japanese government's stored rice has reached more than 2.2 million shi due to years of accumulation. After Japan's efforts to improve agriculture, not only is there no need for foreign rice, but the domestic production is suffering from excess. Recently, the rice market has plummeted by more than one yuan per dou. Also, due to the bumper autumn harvest, the Japanese government, considering that the stored rice is old and unsaleable in the country, is trying to sell it overseas. The price of rice in Shanghai is actually more expensive than Japanese rice, so the Japanese government has decided to ship a large quantity to Shanghai for trial sale. The Japanese Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry has now sent Mr. Katayama and Mr. Sawada to supervise this matter. They have leased two transport ships from Mitsui & Co., one named the Mitsukeyama Maru and the other the Azumayama Maru. The Mitsukeyama Maru will load 5,000 tons of Japanese rice in Kobe on the 11th of this month and ship it to Shanghai, which is expected to arrive around the 15th or 16th of this month. After that, the Azumayama Maru will set sail with 7,000 tons, all of which will be sold in our country. It is heard that each shi will be sold for ten yuan to test the sales in our country. It is hoped that all sectors of our country will pay attention. The Japanese rice shipped to Shanghai is all old. If it can be sold well in Shanghai, then 2.2 million shi of old rice will be shipped to our country, with a total value of 22 million yuan.

The Third National Products Sports Meet Closed Yesterday 111

The Exhibition of Domestically Produced Silks and Satins Was Full of Brocade

More Than 2,000 Guests Filled the Venue Yesterday afternoon at 1 p.m., the closing ceremony of the Third National Products Sports Meet of Shanghai City was held at the City General Chamber of Commerce. At the same time, a national products silk and satin exhibition was opened, and there were Xia Mei amusement tickets and gifts to add to the fun. The guests included Li Xicheng, representative of the Garrison Headquarters; Zhang Dabang, representative of the Second Higher Branch of the Jiangsu High Court; Bao Jun, representative of the Jianghai Customs Supervisory Office; Ye Hongji, representative of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs; representatives of various bureaus of the Municipal Government; and people from the business community, totaling about 2,000 people, filling the venue and leaving no empty seats. The situation on that day is recorded as follows:

Opening Ceremony (1) All stand at attention; (2) Sing the Party song; (3) Pay the highest respect to the Party and National flags and the portrait of the Premier; (4) The Chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; (5) Silence; (6) The Chairman delivers a speech; (7) Speeches; (8) Exhibition; (9) Amusements; (10) Closing.

A Glimpse of the Venue In front of the City General Chamber of Commerce, a long rectangular silk banner read "Shanghai City Third National Products Sports Meet National Products Silk and Satin Exhibition." The venue was in the main hall, and the products of various factories were displayed in the corridors on the second and third floors, totaling more than 100 companies. Silk and satin shops from Hangzhou, Huzhou, Shengze, Suzhou, Shandong, and Henan all had products on display. Dashing, Tianfu, Vida Silk and Satin Store on Shiliu Road, Nanjing Road, Dalun, Dasheng, Lao Jiefu, Lao Jiuzhang, Jiulun, etc., Yong Shenchang, Chunji, Zhengyu, Fengxiang, Zhongxing, Heng Hui, Jishengji, Yuechangwen, Yuesheng, Luo Zhenyuan, Ankang, Zhenya, Cheng Yuyuan, etc., displayed various kinds of yarn, silk, and satin. There were also new men's and women's uniforms made by Yuanyuan Clothing Store, etc., which were full of brocade and beautiful.

Presidium Huang Daozhu Lin, Section Chief of the Municipal Government; Pan Gongzhan of the Social Bureau; Fan Zhengbo of the Municipal Party Department; Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the City General Chamber of Commerce; Wang Yansong and Luo Qinghua of the satin industry.

Director Pan's Speech Today, the Third National Products Sports Meet of Shanghai City is holding a national products silk and satin exhibition at the City General Chamber of Commerce. I am very happy and honored to have you all come to visit. Since the opening of this National Products Sports Meet on the 7th, we have used various methods to promote the practicality of our country's self-made goods, and especially pay attention to clothing materials. Clothing, food, housing, and transportation are the four major needs of life. Therefore, this conference has specially devoted itself to promoting the use of Chinese materials to make clothes. We know that the trade deficit of foreign goods coming to China reaches 400 million yuan per year, that is, each person contributes about one yuan to foreigners every year. At least half or one-third of this amount is used for clothing. It can be seen that the Chinese people are obsessed with foreign clothing materials. Of course, there is no Chinese material for wearing Western clothes, and even those who wear Chinese clothes do not know the benefits of Chinese silk and satin, and they all tend to use foreign goods. We held a national products fashion exhibition at the Dahua Hotel on October 9th. At that time, many famous ladies who participated in the performance wore various costumes made of national product materials. They felt that the quality, color, pattern, and style were all good, and they were noble and precious, and they were by no means inferior to foreign goods. This is witnessed by those who participated in the meeting. However, the conference was biased towards the female community, and due to ticket restrictions, it was unable to extend the invitation to guests, and it was deeply felt that the publicity was not sufficient. Therefore, we specially consulted with the National Products Silk and Satin Industry Association to hold a national products silk and satin exhibition before the closing of today's conference. Please come and visit. You must know that there are many products from various factories. Today's display is only a selection of several types, divided into grades, so that everyone can choose materials according to their living standards and needs, and can also compare them with foreign goods. Because Chinese people often have the psychology of worshiping foreign goods and despising Chinese goods, when they see clothing materials sold on the market, if they are exquisite, they think they are foreign goods. Merchants cater to this psychology and sell them as foreign goods. This erroneous concept can be swept away after visiting today's exhibits. I hope that you will buy national product clothing from now on. If you make silk clothes, you must buy Chinese silk and satin. If you still reject the good silk and satin that China already has and buy foreign silk and satin, such slave-like behavior, I believe you will never do. And I hope that you will not only set an example, but also persuade others to buy Chinese clothing materials together.

Wang Yansong Reports Wang Yansong, representative of the silk and satin industry, reported that today is the Third National Products Sports Meet of the Shanghai Social Bureau, holding a national products silk and satin exhibition, because the conference feels that promoting national products is not limited to silk and satin, but China is based on silk and tea, and large-scale exports. In recent years, the silk and satin industry has declined and is in urgent need of relief. Therefore, we have designated a day for large-scale publicity. In the future, the benefits of revitalization will not only be limited to the silk and satin industry, but all industrial and commercial people who raise silkworms, reel silk, and weave satin will depend on it for survival, which is really related to the national economy and the people's livelihood. Our industry should be very grateful for the enthusiastic promotion of the Social Bureau. However, the promotion of national products cannot be achieved by empty words. Everyone must enthusiastically purchase and love national products, which is patriotism. For example, in a family, parents love their children, and no one abandons their own children and turns to love other people's children. Therefore, loving compatriots is to cherish domestic products. In the future, our industry will work hard to improve the quality of our products to compete with foreign goods, but you must promote and be happy to purchase them in order to achieve practical results, so as not to fail the enthusiasm of the Social Bureau's promotion.

Fan Zhengbo's Speech Fan Zhengbo, representative of the Municipal Party Department, said that Mr. Wang Yansong has already said very frankly the reason why national products should be used for making clothes. This is still limited to purchasing national products. What I want to report to you is the responsibility of merchants in selling national products. We know that in poor rural areas with inconvenient transportation, the clothes and food are all national products. Once you get to the city, foreign goods are everywhere. For example, in the prosperous areas of this city, if you go to various shops, most of them sell foreign goods. Even if you want national products, there is no way to get them. What's more, the patriotism and discernment of ordinary people are not sufficient at all. Therefore, I hope that merchants will take the responsibility of promoting national products, and after selling all the foreign goods in their shops, they will no longer purchase them. If every family does this, even if someone wants to use foreign goods, there will be no place to buy them. Otherwise, if the sellers sell and the buyers buy, then it will be useless to hold this meeting dozens of times.

Other Speeches Finally, Mr. Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the City General Chamber of Commerce, gave a speech, exhorting the guests to resolve to purchase national products and develop industries from now on. If they continue to be perfunctory, the country will not be a country. His words were extremely sincere. Mr. Ye Huijun also gave a speech, exhorting everyone to be of one heart and one mind, to arouse their conscience, to supervise each other, and to reject foreign goods and buy national products from now on. He also used the example of Japanese people not using Chinese goods as a comparison. His words were extremely painful, and the audience was moved.

Sale of Tickets and Gifts Everyone received many daily necessities donated by national product manufacturers, such as towels, butterfly cream, soap, toothbrushes, scented soap, lace, wine, cigarettes, woven pillows, silk, and clothing materials. Special tickets were sold to draw lots and distribute gifts to the guests. Each ticket was half a yuan, and each person was limited to one ticket. A total of 430 tickets were sold. At least two pieces of silk oil worth one yuan can be obtained, and at most silk clothing materials worth 50 to 60 yuan can be obtained. Those who bought tickets were very crowded. All the funds from the sale of tickets were allocated to the Women's Promotion of Goods Association for expenses.

Amusement Programs (1) Lu Xiaowu Sings Spring (Resisting Foreign Goods)

(2) Zhang Ye'er Fang Shuo Comic Play (Abolishing Treaties) (3) Boxing (National Arts Museum) (4) Wang Wu Neng Sings Promoting National Products (5) Singing and Dancing (Artistic Youths) Women's Singing and Dancing Troupe Linyin Kindergarten Resonance Singing and Dancing Troupe Yudie Singing and Dancing Troupe Jingqin Girls' School (6) Boxing and Dancing (Liangjiang Physical Education School)

A Public Notice from the Exhibition Everyone knows that silk and satin are special products of China, with excellent quality, firmness, and durability. Not only are they recognized by the Chinese people as superior clothing materials, but they are also popular all over the world and are a major export of our country. Since Japan, Vietnam, and other countries have imposed harsh taxes on Chinese silk, the foreign trade of Chinese silk has been almost completely blocked. And the ignorant compatriots in the country are plagiarizing the fur of Europeans, wearing Western leather shoes, and desperately acting as salesmen for imperialists. Generally, people are full of foreign goods, wool and flannel, especially in the women's community. There is a feeling that it is not fashionable to wear foreign goods. As this trend grows, the whole country, from top to bottom, is full of foreign air. Therefore, giant ships loaded with foreign goods are about to squeeze through the Wusongkou. The sales of domestic silk and satin have been almost completely plundered. Silk factories have closed down, and farmers and workers have lost their jobs, creating a terrible social situation. The outflow of profits is increasing year by year. The cream and blood of the Chinese Republic flag is almost exhausted. The ambition of imperialist economic aggression is getting higher and higher day by day. This dangerous situation is all caused by the Chinese people's love of using foreign goods and abandoning Chinese silk. Now we can wake up, because since the National Government promulgated the clothing regulations, we know that the national dress is a blue robe and a black mandarin jacket, and the material is limited to domestic silk. Recently, Wang Wu, a diplomatic leader, wore a robe and mandarin jacket to attend international banquets, and all countries praised it very much, which shows that our country's clothing is graceful and worthy of praise all over the world. People who love to wear Western clothes, if they don't know the true beauty and goodness, they must be inferior by nature and act as foreign slaves. Foreign wool and flannel are most likely to hide dirt, and if they are not stored carefully, they will be eaten by frogs and insects, resulting in large holes. Moreover, at this time when gold is expensive and silver is cheap, the value is even more noble. It is far inferior to the cheap and good quality of domestic silk and satin, which are durable and can be washed, dyed, and remade when they are old. Therefore, when it comes to personal economy, we must reject foreign goods and use domestic silk and satin. Women's love of beauty is even greater than that of men. But those who have been to the Dahua Hotel National Products Fashion Exhibition have seen the famous ladies wearing new national silk costumes on that day, how graceful and luxurious, and wealthy. Can foreign clothing materials match it? In order to obtain true beauty and goodness and true economy, we should use domestic silk and satin. In order to resist economic aggression and solve the difficult problems of the national economy and the people's livelihood, we should reject foreign wool and flannel silk and satin, and all imported goods. Compatriots, quickly unite and overthrow foreign wool and flannel, overthrow imported silk fabrics, overthrow imperialist economic aggression, and use domestic silk and satin.

The Dada Steamboat Company Reorganizes 114

Renamed Dada Real Estate Company The local Dada Steamboat Company leased the shoreline of the 16th Pier in Nanshi during the Qing Dynasty to set up a wharf. This year, due to the municipal meeting, the shoreline was reorganized, and it was prepared to give a price to buy the property. The company had previously resolved to comply with the shareholders' meeting and entrusted the board of directors with full authority to handle it. Now, the price that the municipal government should pay has been fully received. Yesterday afternoon, a shareholders' meeting was reconvened at Gongdelin. 29,912 shares were present, totaling 15,272 rights, which was sufficient to meet the statutory number of rights. Mr. Li Yunshu was the chairman, and Mr. Wang Yiting reported on the process. The following resolutions were made: (1) Half of the capital will be returned; (2) The remaining capital will be converted into 500,000 yuan of shares, and a limited liability company will be organized to apply to the government for registration; (3) The old company will be dissolved in accordance with the law, and the new company will be established in accordance with the law. Liu Chengru and Wang Yiting were publicly recommended to handle the matter. The shareholders expressed their gratitude to Mr. Wang Yiting for his hard work in running around and contacting this matter.

Silk Factories Continue to Hold Representative Conference 118

Discussing the Request to the Government to Issue Public Bonds Due to the slump in the silk market and the losses of silk factories, two-thirds of the silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have been shut down. If things continue, all of them will go bankrupt. Representatives have been elected to Shanghai to be responsible for the special handling of the matter, requesting the government to issue 10 million yuan of silk industry public bonds to provide relief to the Chinese silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The first representative conference was held the day before yesterday. Due to the late arrival of the representatives from Wuxi, it was rescheduled to be held yesterday. Yesterday (the 13th) at 3 p.m., the first representative conference was still held at the Shanghai Silk Factory Association. The attendees included Shanghai representatives Shen Huachen, Huang Jinjin, Wang Xiaolai, Zhu Jingan, Wu Shenbo, Huang Jinfan, Zhang Yunsheng, and others, five representatives from Wuxi: Cheng Bingruo, Qian Fenghao, Zhang Zizhen, Yang Yuchu, Xue Shouxuan, and three representatives from Zhejiang: Zhu Mou, Li Youren, Jiang Lanxian. The Wuxi Xin Wuxi Daily dispatched the head of the outside reporter's office, Zhou Hanru, to accompany the delegation to Shanghai to conduct a special interview on the conference agenda, and reported to the newspaper via long-distance telephone so that it could be published today. The Bank of China, considering the importance of the matter, also sent representative Chen Jinren to attend the meeting. They all attended as observers. Shen Huachen was publicly elected as the temporary chairman. The ceremony was performed as usual. First, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, and after visiting Deputy Finance Minister Zhang with representatives Wang Xiaolai and Huang Jinjin to discuss the situation, he submitted the case of whether to request the government to allocate funds to provide relief to our silk factory industry in this autumn of death. The representatives present all believed that it was an urgent necessity to request funds for relief in this disaster of the silk factory industry, and unanimously raised their hands (passed). Next, the amount of relief debt was discussed, and it was resolved to request the issuance of 10 million yuan. Next, the name of the public bond was discussed, and it was resolved to name it the Suzhou-Zhejiang-Shanghai Silk Factory Industry Public Bond. Finally, the distribution and amortization methods of the public bond, as well as the organization of a special committee and other issues were discussed until 7:30 p.m. before the meeting was adjourned.

Deportation of Chinese Many Chinese who went to Japan and were deported by the Japanese authorities are unknown. Recently, there have been Chinese workers working in Mikawashima, Omori-cho Minami, Senju Yamashita-cho, etc. under the Tokyo Prefecture. Special Dispatch from the Yangtze Shipping Industry 121

Emei Asks to Release China Merchants Bureau's Yangtze River Steamer Emei. The Emei was repaired in Shanghai and was scheduled to go to Chongqing, originally intending to make one trip to Shanghai to transport the coffin of Zhao Tieqiao to Sichuan for burial. Yesterday, the bureau received a telegram from Yichang stating that the Emei was seized by the Sichuan army upon arrival in Chongqing for transporting troops between Chongqing and Yichang. The Shanghai bureau was requested to urgently telegraph Liu Xiang for its release. Yesterday, the bureau already telegraphed Sichuan requesting its prompt release.

Datong Establishes a Pontoon. Datong, located in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, is an inland river port where foreign transport cannot dock. To develop commerce and transport in central Anhui and facilitate the loading and unloading of goods and passengers, the Sanbei Company spent sixty to seventy thousand dollars to build a large new pontoon to accommodate the boarding, disembarking, and storage of goods and passengers. It has been completed and towed away. A telegram received yesterday stated that the pontoon has been installed and is ready. From today, Chinese river steamers at Datong can start docking and mooring alongside the pontoon.

Damaged Ships Under Repair. The China Merchants Bureau's steamer Xinchang, which operates on the Yangtze River, telegraphed from Nanjing yesterday stating that its machinery was damaged and it could not navigate. It needs to be towed back to Shanghai for major repairs. Also, the bottom of the Taishun steamer was suddenly damaged, posing a danger. A telegram was sent to Shanghai requesting a ship to be dispatched to tow both ships back to Shanghai for repairs. The bureau has already dispatched a ship to tow them.

Wage Increase Movement for Chinese Seamen on Foreign Ships Nearing Resolution 125

Yu and Chen to Mediate

Seamen Show Flexibility. The case of seamen demanding wage increases from six foreign shipping companies has been repeatedly negotiated by the Seamen's Union with Swire Shipping and other companies without success, as previously reported in this newspaper. It has been learned that Yu Qiaqing and Chen Bogang are mediating in this matter, and both sides are gradually approaching an agreement. Yesterday, this reporter contacted Mr. Wang Yongsheng, the guiding committee member of the union, to learn about the progress of the negotiations and the mediation efforts. Details are as follows:

Negotiation Process. The Seamen's Union sent representatives to negotiate wage increases with Swire, Jardine, and other companies. Swire repeatedly stated that it did not oppose the principle of wage increases but requested a postponement due to poor business this year. As a result, no agreement was reached. On Tuesday of last week, seamen's representatives negotiated this matter with Swire. Swire only agreed to transfer the rice allowance to the wage increase, which was opposed by the seamen. By Double Ten Day, Swire Company, in order to resolve the wage increase case as soon as possible, voluntarily invited Yu Qiaqing and Chen Bogang, the chairman of the Shipping Association, to mediate.

Yu and Chen's Mediation. Entrusted by the British companies, Yu and Chen mediated between labor and management. At 6 PM on the 10th, they went to the Seamen's Union on Qiu Jiang Road to discuss mediation methods with labor representatives. Yu and Chen explained to the representatives that the wages of Swire ships' seamen were slightly higher than other companies and requested some concessions, while Chinese ships would definitely not follow suit. They also hoped for a response that day to facilitate mediation. Yu and Chen then left to await the seamen's reply.

New Plan Resolved. The Seamen's Union convened an emergency meeting of all members on the 11th to discuss how to respond to Yu and Chen's mediation. All members voted to (1) increase the monthly salary of Swire ships, which was already 28.8 yuan, by six yuan after canceling the rice allowance (currently increasing by four yuan, with another two yuan in March of next year).

Now, they are willing to concede one yuan and change it to a one-time increase of five yuan. After the decision was made, a formal letter was immediately sent to Mr. Yu, requesting him to convey it. Since Mr. Yu has gone to Beijing, the matter must wait until his return to Shanghai to be resolved.

Jardine Handles Separately. Regarding the wage increase case for Jardine Matheson's ships, the seamen decided to deal with it separately because the company had hired non-union members and undermined the labor movement during the May 30th Massacre and had also reduced seamen's wages by two yuan (currently only 26.8 yuan). The resolved plan is: (1) The rice allowance should be canceled and six yuan should be added. (2) The two yuan monthly salary deducted during the May 30th incident must be compensated and recalculated to the present. Furthermore, regarding the Nissin Company's ships, because they have not been sincere in their dealings regarding the wage increase issue, it is necessary to negotiate seriously. Therefore, it is necessary to add a full six yuan and absolutely no concessions can be made. This demand has also been put forward.

Hope for Resolution. Yu Qiaqing can forward the seamen's new demands to Swire upon his return to Shanghai from Beijing. According to Wang Yongsheng, the opinions of both sides are close to an agreement regarding the wage increase case for Swire ships. With Yu and Chen mediating, a satisfactory resolution can be expected soon.

Wage Increase for Stewards. The stewards of various ships are also included in this wage increase request. However, for the monthly salaries of stewards, most shipping companies delegate the responsibility to the compradors, which is different from the direct payment of salaries to stokers and sailors. Now that a wage increase has been proposed, the Chinese shipping companies have agreed to increase the salary portion of each ship's steward by 20% starting in August and then by another 10% in March of next year. This matter has been decided by the companies and has already been notified to the ship compradors for implementation.

Active Improvement Plan for the Beijing-Shanghai Railway 126

New-Style Locomotives Ordered for Passenger Trains

Regulations Issued for Compliance. The Traffic Department of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, in view of the increased passenger and freight traffic compared to the past, has increased the number of trains this year to strive for passenger convenience. However, the current locomotives used by the railway are old, and their horsepower is somewhat insufficient, resulting in slightly weaker towing power. Therefore, delays occur immediately when affected by adverse weather conditions. In view of this, the railway ordered six new-style locomotives from the Pacific Company last month. Their towing power is half that of the older ones and are intended for use on passenger trains. The railway is also cooperating with the Railway Affairs Department to actively improve all train operations to ensure that all trains scheduled to depart daily arrive at their stations on time. All stations along the route have also been issued train operation regulations and ordered to comply to avoid unnecessary delays. Stations with incomplete facilities will be immediately set up to ensure that there will be no difficulties in train operations in the future. All of the above plans are being implemented separately. Other improvements will also continue to be implemented in sequence according to the original plan.

Wuhan Opens Wireless Telegraph 127

Receiving and Sending Begins Immediately. Wuhan is located in the middle reaches of the Yangtze River. The Ministry of Communications originally set up a long-wave radio station there to communicate with ships sailing up and down the Yangtze River. However, because it was not connected with short-wave stations in various parts of the country, it could not communicate with each other. Radio stations in various places, except for telegrams to Wuhan requested by the sender to be forwarded by post from Hankou, did not accept them. Now, the Radio Management Bureau, in response to requests from merchants and residents in various places, has submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications to open wireless telegraph service in Wuhan, add equipment to the Wuhan Radio Station, and has notified radio stations nationwide to start receiving and sending commercial telegrams there immediately. From now on, telegrams to Wuhan can be transmitted by radio, which will also be welcomed by merchants in the upper Yangtze River area.

This is to be reviewed and responded to for compliance, etc. We have approved this. Pan Peide's Opinion on Borrowing and Levying Rent 129

Requests Publication of Borrowing and Levying Amounts

And Set Limit at One Million Yuan. Pan Peide, a Shanghai Chinese property owner, submitted a document to the Municipal Government, stating: "Regarding the case of borrowing and levying rent to raise customs treasury bonds, in accordance with the announcement, the main priority is to ensure timely and full amounts. I humbly request that you instruct the micro-collection agencies to announce the amounts at any time, and once the coupon is fully subscribed, immediately stop the micro-levy to show great faith and alleviate the people's hardship. I have investigated that the Central Government issued short-term customs treasury bonds for the 19th year, and this city was ordered to raise one million yuan. After deliberation by your bureau, it was announced that rent would be borrowed and levied for two months, and twelve articles of regulations were stipulated and announced for implementation. Previously, due to military affairs and wars, the Chinese properties in this city had already sacrificed rent and fulfilled their obligations repeatedly. Now, the market is sluggish, property prices have plummeted, and rent arrears are consistently more than half a year. The monthly rental income for those who invest in property is often insufficient to cover the interest on mortgages, and for the elderly, widowed, and weak who rely on rental income for their livelihood, it is not enough to support their families. There are real examples to prove this kind of hardship, and it is deeply heartbreaking to talk about. However, considering that this customs treasury bond is related to the country's military needs, although it is beyond our capabilities, we should reluctantly bear the burden to fulfill our obligations as citizens. However, public opinion believes that since the customs treasury bond is fixed at one million yuan, the rent should also be limited to one million yuan. The regulations stipulate that rent will be borrowed and levied for two months, which is excessive and will inevitably increase the burden. Therefore, property owners do not avoid expressing their opinions to you. I have investigated that in the Republic of China's 16th year, this city levied patriotic donations for two months, also using rent to offset the cost, collecting approximately 1.25 million yuan per month, totaling 2.5 million yuan for two months. Old donation records are available for verification. Based on this, levying rent for one month to offset one million yuan of treasury bonds is sufficient. Furthermore, it is heard that the collection area includes not only the concessions but also all properties in the towns and cities within this city's jurisdiction and the roads built across borders. In addition, rental income has slightly increased in recent years, so levying rent for one month is estimated to be more than one million yuan. Furthermore, I have investigated that this city collects property donations every month, with housing at 10% of the rent and stores at 40% of the rent. The Finance Bureau must have statistics on property donation income and can find out how much monthly rental income is, so it is impossible to be without any certainty. If the numbers are close to the above figures, then levying rent for one month is enough to offset one million yuan of treasury bonds, which is even more credible. For the sake of raising customs treasury bonds, borrowing and levying rent for two months will inevitably result in more than double the quota, and property owners have no extra capacity to bear such a heavy burden. At this time, we only seek to ensure the quota of one million yuan for customs treasury bonds. If levying rent for one month is already sufficient, then the second month can be stopped. Taking a step back, if levying rent for one month is still 200,000 yuan short of the quota, then levying rent for one week in the second month will be sufficient. In short, the amount and time should be calculated proportionally to raise the full quota, and then the micro-levy should be stopped. Therefore, the stipulated two-month period should be considered as a hypothetical period with some room for adjustment. Therefore, we jointly appeal and request that you examine and verify this matter and order the collection agencies to announce the amount of rent collected at any time, and once the quota for customs treasury bonds is raised, immediately stop the micro-levy. In this way, we can maintain faith from top to bottom, which would be beneficial to the overall situation and the property owners. Respectfully submitted."

Child Welfare Association Invites Mrs. Vandervelde to Lecture 131

The Child Research Department of the Chinese Child Welfare Association, in addition to having a committee of experts dedicated to research and publishing a series of books, has repeatedly invited foreign child welfare experts to China to lecture to promote discussion and planning. Survives Five Hours in the Red Sea 133

Chen Jinjiang Angrily Jumps into the Sea

Floats in Water for Five Hours

Catches a Big Fish to Appease Hunger

Rescued by the Huan Ya Steamer. Yesterday, the Huan Ya steamer arrived in port, bringing a novel news story of a Chinese man jumping into the sea in the Red Sea. The story is quite interesting and is described as follows: A man named Chen Jinjiang, from Dinghai, Ningbo, 24 years old, worked as a stoker on the Blue Funnel Line's mail ship Deucalion. The ship sailed from Shanghai to Liverpool, England, on August 18th. In mid-September, while sailing through the Red Sea, Chen Jinjiang asked Wang Fa, the head stoker, for two days of leave due to illness. Wang Fa not only refused to grant him leave but also beat Chen Jinjiang with a rattan stick, forcing him to work while ill. Chen Jinjiang had no choice at the time and, in despair, jumped into the Red Sea to end his life on the morning of September 16th at 10 AM. Surprisingly, he did not drown for five hours and even caught a two-pound fish to appease his hunger. At 4 PM that afternoon, the Huan Ya steamer happened to pass through the Red Sea, and the crew saw Chen Jinjiang floating on the sea surface and quickly rescued him, taking him to Bombay and then to Shanghai yesterday. According to Chen Jinjiang, he plans to return to Ningbo in the coming days and says that he is not good at swimming. As for why he did not drown in the sea for five hours, he does not know either.

Hsing Ting-ch'eng, the Chinese manager of the New Sassoon Company, owner of Qingyun Lane in Hongkou, Shanghai, forcibly ordered tenants to move out unsuccessfully. A Record of the Dance and Variety Show to Benefit the Victims of the Liaoxi Flood 136

Attended by a Sea of People

Variety Show Was Excellent in Every Way. The masquerade ball and variety show held by Dr. Zheng Yuxiu to benefit the victims of the Liaoxi flood started at 9 PM on the evening before last (the 12th) at the Dahua Hotel on Gordon Road. Before 8 PM, the area around Jing'an Temple Road was already filled with cars, and the guests were like a surging tide. By 9 PM, there was no room to stand in the venue. The military band of the Municipal Public Security Bureau played national music to open the event amid applause from the crowd. Then, various programs continued to be performed. Famous ladies in costume danced, some dressed in palace attire, others in theatrical costumes, and they danced gracefully to melodious music, which was quite interesting. The male and female guests in the audience also joined in, and their enthusiasm was very high. Then, students from the Liangjiang Women's Sports School performed dances, which were extremely wonderful. The Datong Music Society, led by Mr. Zheng Qinwen, led the entire group of members to play five pieces of ancient music, and Chinese and foreign guests alike praised them unanimously. This was followed by male and female movie stars jointly performing The Great Grape Fairy, with excellent singing and dancing. After the performance, the association presented Ms. Hu Die with a silver cup and the Mingxing Company with a silver shield to express their gratitude. However, Ms. Hu and the company were willing to auction off the silver shield and silver cup on the spot to help the disaster victims. Mr. Hong Shen raised his glass and called out, and as a result, the silver cup was won by Mr. Zhang Xiaolin for 200 yuan, and the silver shield was won by Mr. Du Yuesheng for 300 yuan. However, after paying, Mr. Zhang and Mr. Du returned the silver cup and silver shield to Ms. Hu and the Mingxing Company to keep as souvenirs. At 1 AM yesterday morning, famous actor Cheng Yanqiu arrived and performed the sword dance from the Red Whisk Girl, which drew thunderous applause. Mr. Cheng also sang a section of "Willow Greets Spring" from Fenhe Bay at the request of the audience, and almost every word was perfect. Mr. Cheng was enthusiastic about helping the disaster relief efforts, and all of his staff did not take any fees, which was especially commendable. It was not until 2:30 AM yesterday morning that the various performances ended, and the audience gradually dispersed, and it was already after 3 AM. It can be said that it was a grand occasion for a time. Also, Dr. Zheng worked extremely hard to organize this event and has suffered a minor illness. She entrusted various parties to sell a large number of tickets, and the ticket money continued to be sent yesterday. Once all the money is collected, it will be remitted to Liaoning to help the disaster victims.

Died While Watching Airplanes 137

Only Cared About Looking Up at the Sky

Did Not Prevent Cars Underground. On Double Ten National Day, airplanes flew in the sky over this city to celebrate. At 11:15 AM on the morning of that day, a countryman named Zhang Ahe, about 42 or 43 years old, was walking on Edward Road, at the intersection of the British and French concessions, when he heard the sound of airplanes in the sky. He looked up while walking in the middle of the road. At that moment, a car No. 161, owned and driven by a British man Huier Sen, residing at No. 78 Albert Road, was driving from the French Concession from east to west. The countryman only cared about looking up at the airplanes in the sky and did not pay attention to the vehicles on the road. The British man's car could not avoid him in time and knocked him down, injuring the back of his head. The British concession police saw this, took down the license plate number, and sent the injured person and car to Renji Hospital for treatment, and reported to the French police for verification. After Zhang was admitted to the hospital, the doctor asked his name and surname, but he could not answer due to coughing. He died at 6:15 PM the following afternoon due to serious injuries and ineffective treatment. The hospital notified the police, who took the body to Tongren Fuyuan Hall for an autopsy. There were no relatives to be found. Yesterday, the Car Affairs Office of the French police summoned the defendant to the station and reported to Judge Zhu Cheng of the French Concession Court, who confirmed that the deceased had been injured by a car and died. He ordered that photos be taken and that the court provide a coffin for burial and placement in the ancestral hall. The defendant was released on bail, and if no relatives come forward within six months, the case will be dismissed. The deceased had a monk's hairstyle, wore a new white twill short shirt and trousers, a new blue cloth shirt, coffee-colored thread socks, and a straight-woven white leather-soled shoe, resembling a rural farmer.

Gang of Kidnappers Busted in Shaoqing Lane 138

Six Robbers Arrested in Succession

A Lot of Military Arms Seized. Detective Xie Shuiquan of the General Police Department learned that a kidnapping gang was organizing a kidnapping plot inside No. 29 Shaoqing Lane on Lafayette Road in the French Concession, holding secret meetings and plotting illegal activities. On the morning of the 11th at 9 AM, he, together with detectives Ma Xiaozhi, Bao Wen, Ding Huaguo, West Detective Mayson, and others, went to the house upstairs with Chinese and Western detectives from the French Police Department and arrested Yang Hua, a resident of Pudong, Monk Hua Quanrui, and Shen Laiyi, four robbers. They seized a pistol, eight live rounds, and eight Mauser bullets in a drawer. They also seized a Mauser pistol and 23 bullets under a wardrobe and brought them to the police station. Later, Yang confessed that his accomplices, Hu Shaoqing from Suzhou and Wang A'er from Shanghai, were at a certain teahouse on Haikou Road. The detectives went again and arrested Hu and Wang. They also seized 200 yuan in cash, 100 yuan in counterfeit money, and gold jewelry and other valuables at Wang's home at No. 871 Dongsheng Lane on Zhejiang Road. They were taken to the police station and sent to the first criminal court of the Special District Court yesterday morning. Police lawyer Ru Bao Yi explained the arrest situation and said that the police had not yet investigated the defendants' crimes, so they were temporarily prosecuting them under Article 161 of the Criminal Law for organizing a criminal gang with the purpose of committing crimes, and also charged the four defendants, Yang, Qin, Hua, and Shen, with violating Article 1 of the Regulations for the Suppression of Military Firearms and requested a 14-day extension for investigation. Yang and Hua confessed that they had previously organized the kidnapping of Jiang from Chunzai Lane on Xinzha Road. The other people gave evasive testimony. Wang A'er even hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Yuan Yangan to defend him. After reviewing the confessions, Judge Sun Yuan ordered all defendants to be returned to custody and rescheduled the hearing.

City National Arts Hall Opens Welcoming New Members Conference 139

Simultaneously Distributing Solicited Prizes

Mr. Zhang Zhijiang Attends and Delivers a Speech: The Shanghai City National Arts Hall held a conference yesterday in the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce assembly hall to welcome new members and distribute solicited prizes. Over two thousand male and female members attended. Mr. Zhang Zhijiang, Director of the Central National Arts Hall, was invited to give a speech. Mr. Zhang Yuejun, Director of the hall (represented by Secretary Cen of the Municipal Government), presided over the meeting. The meeting began at 2:30 p.m. with the ringing of a bell. The chairman delivered a welcome address, stating that the hall was holding a conference to welcome new members and distribute solicited prizes. Seeing such a large number of attendees indicates the excellent results of this solicitation and demonstrates that society is gradually beginning to believe in the value of national arts. This is very gratifying. We know that the efficacy of national arts can strengthen the body and the race, defend the country and protect the people. We hope that the members and guests present today will not only study and practice themselves, but also work hard to promote national arts so that they become widespread throughout the city. Mr. Zhang Zhijiang then gave a speech, stating that he was very pleased to participate in today's grand welcoming event. The Shanghai City National Arts Hall was established shortly after the Central National Arts Hall. There are now nine training grounds and nearly two thousand members, and significant achievements have already been made. I greatly admire and am very happy about this. National arts are the only way to strengthen physical fitness and are of great importance to the country. I attended the Far Eastern Games held in Japan and the results were the worst for our country. In some events, we did not even have a single participant. The weakness of the physical constitution of our citizens and the lack of attention to physical education were evident. This highlights the importance of practicing national arts. We know that to achieve construction, it must start from a spiritual foundation. Without a healthy body and an enthusiastic spirit, nothing can be accomplished. Therefore, national arts are the foundation of the Party and the country. Currently, bandits are rampant in provinces such as Henan, committing murder, kidnapping, and all sorts of evils. The people, lacking the ability to resist, are forced to submit and suffer their ravages. In this kind of situation, unless military police are stationed everywhere to protect them, which is not practically possible, our Premier said that individuals, groups, and countries must have the ability to defend themselves in order to survive. Conversely, without the ability to defend oneself, one cannot survive. We must have the ability to defend ourselves, and the only way to do this is for everyone to practice national arts. When I went to Japan, I saw that the country placed great emphasis on physical education, regardless of whether they were farmers, workers, or merchants. Our national arts are unique in the world. This is our national essence, our treasure. We must promote and develop this national essence and treasure. The meaning of today's conference is not only to welcome you all, but also to hope that you will go back and encourage your brothers, children, sisters, relatives, and friends to practice national arts. Mr. Chen Jiaxuan, a director, then reported on the solicitation process, stating that the hall has been established for almost three years. The second solicitation increased by 20% compared to the first, and the third solicitation increased by 30% compared to the second. This is a very good sign. However, considering the population of Shanghai, it is still less than one-thousandth of the population. Therefore, we must continue to work hard to make national arts more and more popular every day. After the report, the chairman distributed the solicited prizes. The first prize for each team went to the Unity Team, the second to the Freedom Team, and the third to the People's Rights Team. The individuals with the best performance were Zhu Jiangguang, Tong Zhongyi, and Du Yuesheng. Those with excellent performance were Ye Qichang. Following this, the hall's instructors and students from various training grounds performed national arts. The Magic Spirit Illusion Society's Liang Tian magic troupe performed magic, and the Art and Music Dance Society's sister dance troupe and the New China Music and Dance Society performed dances, all of which were exceptionally wonderful and met with thunderous applause. The meeting adjourned around 7:00 p.m.

Regulations for Dancers' Business in Dance Halls 140

Formulated by the Municipal Government

Registered by the Public Security Bureau: The Municipal Government, due to the frequent presence of underage girls as dancers in dance halls in the city, and the occurrence of inappropriate behavior by dancers during business hours, specifically requested the Municipal Public Security Bureau to formulate regulations for the registration and business of dancers in dance halls in order to curb these issues. It is learned that these regulations have been promulgated by the Municipal Government and are recorded as follows: Article 1: All women who engage in dancing for business within the city must uniformly apply to this Bureau for registration. Article 2: To apply for registration, an application form must first be obtained and completed in duplicate according to the following items, along with two recent 2.5-inch half-body photographs, and submitted to this Bureau for review: 1. Name, 2. Age, 3. Native place and current address, 4. School graduated from, 5. Where dancing was learned, 6. Family situation, including the name and occupation of the husband if married, 7. Current business location and name of the dance hall and the name of the owner. Article 3: After registration is approved, a registration certificate and badge will be issued. The dance hall where the dancer is located shall prepare a registration fee of two yuan and stamps and collect them on behalf of the dancer. Article 4: The badge must be worn on the left side of the clothing during business hours. Article 5: Women under the age of sixteen shall not engage in dancing for business. Article 6: Business hours must comply with the provisions of Article 6 of the Shanghai Municipal Dance Hall Business Regulations. Article 7: When changing occupations, the registration certificate shall be submitted to the dance hall where the dancer is located, and forwarded to this Bureau for cancellation. Article 8: If a dancer works in dance hall A and also in dance hall B, or changes to another dance hall, the owner shall promptly report this in writing to the district office in charge, which shall forward it to this Bureau. Article 9: If a dancer engages in inappropriate behavior during business hours, they will be investigated and dealt with according to the facts of the offense. Article 10: Violations of the provisions of Article 1 or Article 5 of these regulations shall be subject to a fine of up to fifteen yuan and suspension of business. Article 11: Violations of the provisions of Article 7 of these regulations shall be subject to a fine of up to ten yuan. Article 12: Violations of the provisions of Article 4 or Article 9 of these regulations shall be subject to a fine of up to five yuan. Article 13: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation after approval by the Municipal Government.

Ordering Pharmacies to Use the Gregorian Calendar for New and Full Moon Discounts 143

The Shanghai Municipal Party Department Executive Committee recently noted that pharmacies in this city still offer discounts of 10% or 20% on the days of the new and full moon according to the abolished lunar calendar, which is contrary to the principle of promoting the Gregorian calendar. Therefore, it specifically submitted a request to the Central Party Department to forward it to the National Government, requesting instructions to the Executive Yuan to order the Shanghai Municipal Government to order all pharmacies in the city to no longer use the abolished lunar calendar for discounts in the future, but to uniformly use the Gregorian calendar for the new and full moon each month, so that the people's psychology of adhering to the Gregorian calendar can be positively influenced. Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Government received instructions from the Executive Yuan and has transferred the order to the Social Affairs Bureau to forward it to the Pharmaceutical Industry Association for distribution to all colleagues to comply with.

Repair of the Yantai-Dalian Submarine Cable 145

Unimpeded Communication between Shanghai and Dalian: Dalian is an important town in the Northeast, and its commercial prosperity is the crown of Northeast China. Therefore, telegraphic communication is very important. Telegrams sent from this city to Dalian have always been transmitted by the China Telegraph Administration. Because the Administration's line between Yantai and Shanghai is a new submarine duplex line, and the Yantai-Dalian line is also a duplex line, telegrams sent to Dalian only take about ten minutes. Third-class urgent telegrams can arrive in a few minutes. The Administration receives and sends over a thousand telegrams to Dalian every day. However, since the Yantai-Dalian submarine cable broke on the 27th of last month, telegrams to Dalian have been rerouted through Tianjin, Liaoning, and other bureaus. The roundabout transmission has inevitably been delayed, which has inconvenienced merchants and residents. According to news from the China Telegraph General Administration yesterday, the submarine cable between Yantai and Dalian was repaired yesterday (the 13th) morning. Telegrams to Dalian can now be delivered within ten minutes as usual. Anyone wishing to send telegrams can directly contact the China Telegraph General Administration on Sichuan Road in this city, the Shanghai Telegraph North Bureau behind the Jiande Savings Society on Fusheng Road in Zhabei, the Shanghai Telegraph South Bureau at Xiaodongmen in Nanshi, the China Telegraph General Administration sub-receiving office inside the Shanghai Bank at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Tongfu Road, or the China Telegraph General Administration sub-receiving and sending office inside the Shanghai Bank in Tilanqiao.

Verdict on Russian Relief Society Members Gambling 146

Inside the Russian Disabled Relief Society at 172 Bazilu Road, members and outsiders were gambling. The Hongkou Police Department broke up the gambling and arrested 31 Russians, 5 British, 19 Japanese, and 1 Portuguese woman. Gambling paraphernalia, including a dice shaker, playing cards, and over 40 taels of silver foreign currency, were confiscated. The British, Japanese, and Portuguese gamblers were taken away by their respective consulates for punishment. The 31 Russians were sent to the Special Court for interrogation. The case has now concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide visited the Criminal Court No. 3 and sentenced the defendants Fosilin, Temilifu, Yierying, Ximing, Shakao Kao Fu, and Saituo Napin Sike to four months of imprisonment, suspended for two years, for jointly intending to profit from providing a gambling venue. The remaining one thousand Russians, including Xuelifu, were each fined thirty yuan. If they are unable to pay, they will be detained for one day for every two yuan. The gambling paraphernalia and gambling money will be confiscated. The defendants were warned not to repeat the same offense, or they would be severely punished without leniency.

Zhu Zhongrong Splashes Caustic Soda Out of Revenge 149

Former Lovers Now Bitter Enemies - Twice Gathering Crowds to Splash Caustic Soda

Ah Zhen, the eldest daughter of the Shen Zhu family, a Shaoxing woman residing at No. 2018 Xinzha Road, is 29 years old and beautiful. In the spring of this year, she formed an inseparable bond with Zhu Zhongrong, and they rented a house to live together. Zhu provided Shen Zhu with forty yuan per month. Later, Zhu's business closed down, and he became financially strained, unable to afford the monthly payment of forty yuan. Ah Zhen was taken back by her mother, who forbade her from associating with Zhu. Zhu harbored resentment and sought to harm them. On June 6th of this year, at around 7:00 a.m., he gathered a crowd of people and suddenly went to their house, splashing nitric acid indiscriminately, causing injuries to the mother and Ah Zhen. Zhu then fled. However, his heart was still not satisfied. On the 5th of this month, at around 2:00 p.m., Zhu gathered over twenty hooligans and stormed into the Shen Zhu family's house. One person hit the mother's body with an iron bar, and another held Ah Zhen's head, while Zhu poured caustic soda on her, causing severe injuries to Ah Zhen. The mother's face was also affected. Zhu and the others then fled in the chaos. Someone reported this to the Xinzha Police Station, who sent the mother and Ah Zhen to the hospital for treatment. The police then ordered Chinese and Western detectives to arrest the suspects Xu Liansheng, Wang Weixiang, Zhang Huangguang, Li Zigang, Chen Ruilin, and Yang Liubao in room 43 of the Pacific Hotel on Guangxi Road on the day before yesterday afternoon. The main criminal, Zhu Zhongrong, was still at large. They were all taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Second Criminal Court of the Special District Local Court. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the case, claiming that Shen Ah Zhen had been severely injured and was still in the hospital for treatment, requesting an extension. The plaintiff, Shen Zhu, also filed a complaint, explaining the previous situation and identifying the defendants Xu Liansheng and Wang Weixiang as having come with Zhu both times. This time, Xu hit me with an iron bar, Wang held my daughter's head, and Zhu poured caustic soda. Shen Baozhen, Shen Zhu's adopted daughter, testified that she was fourteen years old and sick at home on the 5th of this month, and witnessed Xu, Wang, and the fifth defendant Chen Ruilin being present. When questioned, the defendants all denied the charges. Only Wang Weixiang confessed that Zhu Zhongrong was his friend, and that Zhu and three others went together that day. The caustic soda was poured by someone else, and his arm was also burned. Judge Wu Tingqi verified the confessions and ordered the six defendants to be detained for further questioning in seven days.

Yesterday afternoon at around 2:00 p.m., because the workers' products were substandard, he personally walked into the machine room to inspect whether the motor was damaged. Seen from Various Knife Wounds

Dispute Over a Boatwoman Causing Injury 157

Sun Huaiyou, 37 years old, and his wife Wang, 33 years old, from Yancheng County, Jiangbei, usually drove a cargo boat to transport sweet potatoes to make a living. At around 8:00 p.m. the night before, Sun anchored his boat in the Rihui Bridge port and was about to prepare for bed when a coal barge rushed in from behind. Due to careless driving, the bow of the barge hit the stern of Sun's boat. With a loud crash, the hull of the boat was damaged, and his wife Wang, who was sitting in the stern, was injured in the shoulder and other places, which was very serious. Sun grabbed the boatman of the barge, Zhang A'da, and went to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Shui Third Division. After a brief hearing by the patrol officer, the case was transferred to the Municipal Headquarters yesterday. Under questioning, Sun and others explained the previous situation. Zhang, 31 years old and from Changshu, confessed that the tide was rapid at the time, and he could not hold it, so he unintentionally hit Sun's boat. The police ordered a document to be prepared and submitted to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Fine for Selling Counterfeit Foreign Wine 158

French merchant Longdong Company previously hired a lawyer to represent them in the Criminal Court of the French Concession, accusing Westerner Tu Mengchuanfu and Wensidengnan of counterfeiting the plaintiff's foreign wine and selling it abroad, requesting investigation and compensation for losses. The defendant also hired a lawyer to defend them. It was ordered that the debate should conclude and await verification and judgment. The previous report has been recorded. Yesterday was the date of the verdict. Both parties were summoned to the court. The Chinese and Western judges ruled that the two defendants were found guilty of counterfeiting. The first defendant was fined 50 foreign dollars, and the second defendant was fined 30 foreign dollars. They were also jointly liable for 800 foreign dollars in compensation for the plaintiff's losses to serve as a warning.

Fine of Twenty Yuan for Privately Selling Opium 159

Zhao A'yu, from Ningbo, recently transported a bag of opium, weighing 74 pounds and valued at 4,000 foreign dollars, from another port to Shanghai. While hiring a car at the Bund Wharf in the French Concession to transport it, he was discovered by Chen Sanlin, an investigator of the French Police Department, and detectives Mao Jinsheng and Lu Jinchen. They stepped forward to arrest Zhao and brought him to the police station. Yesterday, he was sent to the French Court for investigation. The head of the police station first reported the previous situation and presented the opium to the court. When questioned, Zhao confessed to the private sale of opium. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Zhao to a fine of 2,000 foreign dollars to be confiscated, and the opium was confiscated.

Copper Coins Smuggled from Jiangbei to Shanghai 160

Recently, the market prices of copper coins in various ports have differed. For example, in Jiangbei, one silver dollar can be exchanged for many copper coins. Carrying them to Shanghai and exchanging them for others can yield a profit of dozens of coins. Therefore, profit-seeking people often take the opportunity to smuggle them in hopes of making a large profit. The authorities in Shanghai have always strictly prohibited the private sale of copper coins. If it is not strictly prohibited, it will affect the market. Therefore, it has been ordered that strict prohibition be enforced. However, there are still many people who smuggle them at risk. Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 p.m., Xu Fuzhou, a guard at the seventh post of the first division of the first district of Nanshi, saw Zhao Dingyu, a clerk from the Fukang Cigarette and Paper Shop at No. 149 Zhoujin Road in the city, transporting over 300,000 copper coins at the Wanyu Wharf. Observing the shape of the packages, he knew that they were smuggled from Jiangbei to Shanghai. He was immediately taken back to the station and ordered to be detained for preliminary review and handling.

Social Affairs Bureau Strictly Prohibits Hooligans from Disturbing Bookbinding Operations 161

Joint Proclamation with the Public Security Bureau

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter yesterday to the Shanghai Bookbinding Industry Association, stating: "We received a letter stating that hooligans broke into bookbinding workshops to tease female workers and requested that the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the Public Security Bureau issue a proclamation strictly prohibiting such behavior. We immediately forwarded the request for investigation and handling. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau approved the request in its No. 2728 approval. After the Public Security Bureau returns the jointly signed proclamation for verification and judgment, it will be sent back for transfer to the association to print and send it to the Bureau for joint printing and distribution."

Court Autopsy Report 163

Chen San: On the morning of the 11th of this month, Lu Zhisun drove a No. 16741 truck carrying goods east on Huade Road. Chen San, a worker on the truck, accidentally dropped the hat he was wearing in the wind, looked down to find it, and carelessly fell to the ground and was severely injured. He was helped to Tongren Hospital, where he died shortly after. The corpse was sent to the autopsy room. Yesterday morning, Xu Mei, the prosecutor from the Special District Court, went to the station to identify the corpse. He ordered that it be handed over to the corpse's mother, Chen Luo, for burial. If she requested compensation, she could file a lawsuit with the court in accordance with the law.

Ji A'lin: Sun Shaokun, a detective from the Harbin Police Department, arrested Ji A'lin and other bandits in 1927 and handed them over to the former Provisional Court, which sentenced them to twelve years of imprisonment. Recently, Ji fell ill and was sent to the hospital for treatment, where he died at 10:00 a.m. on the morning of Double Ten Festival of this month. The corpse was taken by a coffin carrier to the autopsy room on Feilun Road. Yesterday, Prosecutor Xu from the Special District Local Court went to the station for identification. Because no relatives were found, he ordered the Pushan Villa to provide a coffin for burial.

Two Lost Boys Awaiting Claim 164

Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, two lost boys were discovered at the Qichang Machine Wharf in Pudong by patrol officers from the Third District Police Station. After questioning, one identified himself as Ma Kotao, 10 years old, from Tongzhou; the other as Liu Xiaowang, 15 years old, from Shandong. Both claimed to be orphans with no relatives and were thus wandering the streets. The District Chief, noting the recent surge in child abduction cases in Shanghai and fearing they might fall into the hands of criminals for trafficking, ordered a formal request to be sent to the General Bureau for relief.

Fire at Pingliang Road the Night Before 165

The newly opened Zhenxing Noodle Restaurant near the Eight Lane Head Small Vegetable Market on Pingliang Road in Yangshupu experienced a fire the night before. The unextinguished coal stove caused smoke to fill the shop overnight, severely poisoning the staff. Two of them, Tian Jiafu and Jiang Qiangshang, died before medical assistance could arrive. The patrol division dispatched detectives to send the bodies to the Forensic Examination Office on Fei Lun Road. Yesterday morning, Xu Mei, a prosecutor from the Special District Local Court, was commissioned to examine the bodies, confirm their identities, and question Jin Dashi, the owner of the noodle restaurant. Subsequently, Tian Jiaxing and Jiang Caibo, relatives of the deceased, filed reports requesting the release of the bodies. Mr. Xu verified their statements and instructed that the bodies be handed over to Tian Jiaxing and Jiang Caibo for encoffining and burial after they provided written guarantees.

Petty Thugs Run Rampant 166

On the 10th at noon, a petty thug known as "Little White Eyes" at the Xia Hai Temple (intersection of Kunming Road and Maohai Road) attempted to freeload at a squid stall, also behaving inappropriately towards the stall owner's wife. When she refused, he became violent. A passerby, Mr. Jia, intervened but was attacked by Little White Eyes and his gang, including "Little Scabies," "Little Ningbo," and "Little Cobbler," totaling over ten individuals. Mr. Jia suffered a head injury. The patrol officers arrived and only managed to apprehend Little Scabies. These thugs are well-connected, resulting in his release after only two hours of detention. It is rumored that his gang is resentful and intends to demand fifty yuan from the squid vendor as compensation for their losses, otherwise, they will not allow him to set up his stall again.

The Wenhua Readers' Social Gathering Hangzhou Tour, organized by Wenhua Fine Arts Books and Printing Company, with a total of over three hundred participants, departed from the North Shanghai Railway Station on the 11th. At 5:00 PM, they returned to Shanghai by car. It is reported that the Wenhua's grand event only charged five dollars per member, making it the most economical travel option.

Flour Magnate Xu Wenbin Passes Away 168

Market Closed for One Day

Mr. Xu Wenbin, a native of Shaoxing, who initiated the establishment of the Flour Exchange and served as its Vice Chairman for many years, passed away. In the eighth year of the Republic [1919], he founded the exchange. At that time, China had no such enterprise. The Flour Exchange's establishment and flourishing business led to a wave of imitations, creating a significant trend. The fact that only the Flour Exchange survived is attributed to Mr. Xu's efforts. Mr. Xu also held key positions in Shen Da Flour Company and various banks, causing him great anxiety and exhaustion. Last autumn, he lost his eyesight. He stayed home for treatment, but it was to little avail. Last Saturday, he suddenly suffered a stroke, leading to his death yesterday morning at the age of fifty-two. The Flour Exchange, in recognition of his great contributions, has decided to close the market for one day today as a tribute to his memory.

Lili Company Sells Local Produce Vigorously 169

The Fengjing Ding Yixing's Ding Hoof and Tendons have always been famous. To increase the culinary delights of Shanghai residents, Lili Company specifically dispatches personnel every morning to Fengjing to transport the fresh and delicious products to Shanghai via early trains.

Xie Ji Leather Goods Store, located south of the Tong Xiexiang Seafood Store in the Throw Ball Field area, opened yesterday. The interior was neatly arranged, and the hospitality was gracious. Therefore, the opening day's business was the most prosperous among its peers.

Special Feature

A Thank You to the Gentlemen Who Sponsored the National Goods Movement (Third Continuation) Pan Gongzhan 175

It is even clearer that the trend in the industrial and commercial sectors has reached a critical point. Of the cases in the 17th year [1928], those arising from wage issues numbered 27, three more than those related to layoffs. Cases related to working hours numbered 8. In the 18th year [1929], wage cases still numbered 26, but disputes over employment or layoffs had increased to 36, while working hours cases had decreased to only one. This shows that after the labor struggles in the 16th and 17th years, the increase in wages and the reduction in working hours had reached a considerable level. Beyond this limit, the capitalists were truly unable to cope and had no choice but to reduce the scope of their operations or simply close down. As a result, cases of disputes and strikes arising from layoffs naturally increased. In the 17th year, the percentage of cases where labor's demands were fully accepted as a result of strikes and shutdowns reached 38.47%, but this decreased to 28.83% in the 18th year. On the other hand, the percentage of cases where labor's demands were not recognized was only 10.25% in the 17th year, but this increased to 28.83% in the 18th year. This is certainly due to the gradual improvement in the capitalists' negotiating abilities, but the capitalists' business situation was truly on the verge of collapse, and the situation had reached a point where it could not be further aggravated. Therefore, there was this phenomenon. In other words, the industrial and commercial sectors of Shanghai, after the wave of labor unrest in the 16th and 17th years, had almost reached a dead end in the 18th year, with no room for maneuver. The capitalists had no choice but to do their best to contend with labor in the last moments of breath in order to survive, or simply resign themselves to fate and allow their businesses to shut down. Since the 14th year of the Republic [1925], national goods factories had been gradually gaining momentum for two or three years, but this setback was an undeniable disaster. Fifth, the pain felt by the industrial and commercial sectors is naturally due to the heavy and complex taxes. For example, the cocoon tax in the 2nd year of the Republic [1913] was only six yuan per load of dried cocoons, but recently it has increased to 13.5 yuan per load in Zhejiang, 12.5 yuan per load in Jiangsu, and 10.5 yuan per load in Anhui, an increase of about 100%. Another example is tea. Taking Huizhou tea as an example, the freight cost for transporting raw tea to Shanghai is 3.4 yuan per load, in addition to the manufacturing cost of 21.5 yuan, and the tax is 6.81 yuan. For boxed tea, the manufacturing cost is 10.84 yuan per load, and the freight is 2.8 yuan, with a tax of 2.36 yuan. The heavy production costs can be imagined. Another example is cigarettes. Chinese merchants feel the pain of the cigarette tax scale very deeply. According to the scale, there are seven grades. The sixth grade, with a selling price of over 128.81 yuan per case, has a tax of 53.625 yuan. The seventh grade, with a selling price of under 128.81 yuan per case, has a tax of 29.250 yuan. Most of the products produced by Chinese merchants only pay taxes at the sixth and seventh grades, with lower selling prices, and very few pay taxes at the fourth and fifth grades. The most painful thing is that the cost of raw materials has increased and expenses have increased, making the cost already high. But if the selling price is slightly increased by several yuan per case, the tax must change from the seventh grade to the sixth grade, requiring an additional tax of more than 20 yuan. If the market price is increased, sales will inevitably decrease significantly. Another example is silk fabrics. When exporting overseas, foreign governments levy heavy taxes. Without even considering that, in the country alone, the Guancheng Hall in Hangzhou donated 120,000 yuan annually before the 16th year of the Republic [1927], for a total of 160,000 yuan including water conservancy donations. Now it has increased to 480,000 yuan annually, a threefold increase. There is no need to continue the recitation. Another example is cotton textiles. In the 15th year of the Republic [1926], the import tax on yarn was 5%, and the import tax on cloth was 5.75%. In the 18th year [1929], it was uniformly 7.5%. The average estimated price of taxable goods also increased by 20% to 30%, which is equivalent to a tax increase. In addition, there is the likin tax. Each load of yarn had to pay 56 cents in the 15th year [1926] and 74 cents in the 18th year [1929], which also increased costs. Another example is the nitrate ore used in matches. Chinese merchants must pay a bill of lading fee of 6.5 yuan for every 5,000 catties, while foreign merchants are exempt. When their finished products leave the factory, national goods must pay likin and miscellaneous taxes. For example, in provinces such as Fujian and Sichuan, the miscellaneous taxes (excluding the regular tax) must be paid at more than half of the goods' price per case, while foreign matches do not require this. All of these are just a few examples that are commonly seen. The heavy and complex taxes are obviously evident, and the unequal treatment between Chinese and foreign merchants simply promotes the suicide of national goods factories. Sixth, we should naturally consider the blows that military disasters and bandits have given to the agricultural, industrial, and commercial sectors. China, a country based on agriculture, has a sad trend of relying on foreign countries for large agricultural products, which has been thoroughly discussed by Mr. Zhu Yinong, Tao Xisheng, Feng Ziming, and others. Due to the decline of agricultural products and the bankruptcy of rural areas, there are more soldiers and bandits. Due to the increase in soldiers and bandits, transportation is more obstructed and industries are more weakened. Looking around the country, thanks to the gifts of warlords and communists, there is almost no quiet place to live, let alone work happily. The losses that these military disasters and bandits have given to the industrial and commercial sectors cannot be calculated in numbers. If there is no way to effectively achieve unity and peace, the industrial and commercial sectors have absolutely no way to survive. Seventh, we must talk about the weaknesses of national goods factories themselves. The lack of capital concentration and the lack of cooperation between labor and capital have already been mentioned. In addition, most of the leaders have outdated minds and lack of knowledge. They neither know how to find talent nor do they know how to manage scientifically. They neither respect business ethics nor do they know how to cooperate. Except for a few with new ideas who can cope with this difficult environment, they are either acting impulsively or sighing helplessly, so that they are struggling to break out of this oppressive atmosphere (to be continued).

To the esteemed editors, I recently read in the local news section of today's newspaper an item about the formation of an organization for the blind, which mentioned "Zhang Wenhuan, a translator at the Continental Newspaper who is blind." Upon investigation, the blind translator at the Continental Newspaper is the undersigned, Zhang Wenhui. There is no Zhang Wenhuan. The name is incorrect, presumably due to a misunderstanding. I am writing to request a correction to reflect the facts. I wish you well. Zhang Wenhui, resident at 468 Julaida Road, October 12th.

As these are important matters, we respectfully request that you publish this letter in the Letters to the Editor column. If the owners can provide the deed number and details of the promissory note, our association will return the items. We earnestly request that you publish this. The Shanghai Garment Workers' Union, October 13, 1929.

According to him, his name is Xu Jincai, he is eight years old, from Shanghai, his father's name is Qipu, he is a plasterer, his mother, elder brother, and aunt live near the Old West Gate in the Chinese Concession. We request that you publish this in the local news section of your newspaper to facilitate claiming. Thank you for your kindness. The Model Rural Affairs Office of Yingqian, Fujian, October 4th.

To the esteemed editors, our client, Weng Zhenchu, the owner of the Qingxing Pawnshop, has stated that in the local news section of your newspaper on the 8th of this month, there was a news item stating that the home of Zhang Genfa at 288 Laohuo Road was robbed last month. It stated that the entire amount was pawned at Qingxing Pawnshop at 113 Datong Road, Zhabei. Yesterday morning, detective Song Bingzheng and others from the police station went to the Fourth District of Zhabei, and, along with the pawnshop owner Chen Meichun, found countless stolen goods while arresting Wang Hanwen. The suspects were taken back to the police station. In fact, during the police investigation, no stolen goods were found in the pawnshop. Court records can be checked. Please correct the newspaper on behalf of our client. We request that this is corrected in the newspaper. Respectfully submitted to the chief editor of Shen Bao. Lawyer Wu Chengyu, October 13th.
